The medical team disembarked first, rushing past your squad to secure the lounge and recover the fallen. Their white and dark cyan uniforms stood out against the dark, grimy interior of the building. Then came the reinforcements, stepping out of the second VTOL. Among them was a familiar face, the woman who had tried to speak with you back at the base. If she recognized you, she didn’t show it. There was no time for personal connections here. The sergeant wasted no time, gesturing to the group. “We’re moving. This block has more rooms to clear, but they’re smaller. Stick together. I don’t want another damn surprise.” Maria adjusted her grip on her smg, and stepped forward. “I’ll support Sierra’s lead. I can handle close quarters.” The sergeant paused, turning to face her. He studied her for a moment, then nodded approvingly. “Good enthusiasm. Fall in.” The squad was on the move, boots against the carpet as you advanced to the next apartment rooms. She fell in beside you, her presence oddly comforting despite the circumstances. Her silence wasn’t hostile, it felt deliberate, respectful. As you ascended the narrow stairwell, her voice broke the quiet. It wasn’t directed at you, not entirely, but it was clear she was speaking to herself. “You know, I’ve seen plenty of missions like this. People on both sides thinking they’re doing what’s right. It’s just… messy. Always messy.” You didn’t respond. Room by room, you and your team swept through the apartment complex. Each door opened to reveal lives interrupted, fear etched onto faces, and hasty explanations from civilians who wanted nothing more than for you to move on. Most rooms were empty of contraband, the occupants compliant and silent. Occasionally, sharp bursts of gunfire came from other squads. Reports of "flatlines" came through the comms as anti-Federals tried to resist, drawing weapons they couldn’t hope to use fast enough. The sound of pulse rifles discharging, followed by confirmations of termination under the Federation's strict doctrines. The woman was quieter now, her earlier confidence seems to have depleted. You didn’t look at her directly. A flickering yellow dot materialized over one of the apartment doors, hovering in your HUD like a persistent priority. It was subtle, almost ghostly in its presence. Last objective for this floor. “Let’s make this quick,” Rowan muttered, his voice even, devoid of any emotion beyond duty. Maria gave a small nod, gripping her MP5 a little tighter as the two approached the door. **[[BREACH.]]**Rowan mule kicked the door open, the loud noise of splintering wood making the occupants inside flinch. There was a faint smell of old cooking oil, and lighting that gave everything a light blue tint. The couple inside, a man and a woman in their early twenties, froze. “Stay right there,” Rowan ordered. He motioned for Maria to stay by them. “Watch them. I’ll clear the place.” She hesitated for half a second, trying to soften the situation. “Hey, relax,” she said, her tone warm but with an pinch of nervousness. She lowered her MP5 slightly, her body still tense but her words more approachable. “It’s just a safety check, nothing to worry about. Loyalists reported this building had… well, a lot of armed folks. There’s been trouble. A couple FedSec officers were killed here.” The couple exchanged a look, fear still there, but her words seemed to dull the sharp edge of their panic. The woman, dressed in an oversized sweater, looked Maria up and down, her look of fear softening. “You’re really pretty” the woman blurted, almost like it slipped out before she could stop herself. “Oh, Thank you!” she said quickly, her voice slightly higher than usual. She glanced back at Rowan, who was already rifling through drawers in the small kitchenette, oblivious to the exchange. The man also seated on the couch, cleared his throat. “We’re not armed. We’re just trying to live here, same as everyone else.” She offered a small, strained smile. “I get it. Just… stay calm, alright? This’ll be over in no time.” Rowan moved through the apartment, pulling open closets, flipping through cabinets, and checking under furniture. To the grunt, it was unsettling how little he seemed to care about the people in the room. ''Then he found something.'' In a drawer beneath a clutter of receipts and loose change, your hand paused. It wasn’t a weapon, no, it wasn’t even remotely dangerous, but your grip tightened as you pulled it out. A small stack of worn papers, the edges frayed from frequent handling. Propaganda. Anti-Federal pamphlets, the kind that could get you killed just for possession. Your face remained still as you held them up. “Found something.” You called. The grunts heart sank as she glanced over at him, then at the couple. The woman’s eyes widened in terror, her hand instinctively reaching for the man’s arm. “What—what is that?” the man stammered, his voice shaking. You stepped back into the main room, tossing the papers onto a small coffee table. “Care to explain this?” you asked. The couple looked at the papers, then at each other. The man opened his mouth to respond, but no words came out. The woman clutched his arm tighter, tears beginning to well in her eyes. The grunt could feel the tension in the room, she couldn't bear to just stay there silently. “Rowan,” she started, her voice low, almost pleading. You didn’t respond, your eyes fixed on the couple. The thunderhead’s directives buzzed faintly in his mind, a subtle but constant presence. Loyalists were right. Anti-Federal material confirmed. Civilian compliance protocol applies. The man finally found his voice. “That’s not ours! Someone must have planted it! We don’t.. we’re not part of anything!” Your expression didn’t change. “Doesn’t matter whose it is. It was here. That’s enough.” The grunt stepped between you and the couple, her body language defensive, her voice firm but still trembling slightly. “Wait, hold on. This… this doesn’t mean they’re guilty of anything. Maybe they don’t even know what it is.” Your eyes went to her. “Protocol doesn’t care about ‘maybe,’ Grunt. You know that. Get out of my way or I will also terminate you for insubordination.” The couple clung to each other, the woman sobbing now, her voice cracking as she begged. “Please, we didn’t do anything! We swear!” Maria turned back to Rowan, her expression desperate. “They’re scared out of their minds, Rowan! This isn’t justice, this is—” “Duty.” Rowan interrupted. He raised his wrist communicator. “Priority evidence retrieved. Awaiting orders.” The grunts heart sank as she realized how far gone he was. To him, this wasn’t a moral choice, it was procedure, nothing more. The transmission, a harsh, series of clicks and hisses. A sound you couldn’t place, until you understood. A deep guttural resonance, almost like a distant of some long-forgotten language. But then it became clearer. **“Vncthy’r i’nto’thak. Ktnsh’th k’rrt-lu frn’ash.”** It was as if the words had always been there, waiting for you to understand. They made sense, not in any way human, but undeniably clear. **Terminate anti-federals.** The words burned in your chest. You barely even processed the couple in front of you anymore. They were just targets now. You felt the presence of the Thunderhead in your mind, like a voice in the back of your skull whispering that you had no choice, that this was the only way. You could see the fear in their eyes, the trembling of their hands, but it didn’t matter. They had already been marked. The woman’s shaking voice broke through, “Please… please don’t…” But you didn’t hear her. The Thunderhead whispered its orders, and you obeyed, moving toward them. It wasn’t that you didn’t see them anymore. It was just that you couldn’t feel them, couldn’t hear them. The woman looked at Maria for a brief moment, then back to you. Her voice trembled, almost a whisper as she said, “She… she’s so beautiful. I.. I can’t even… imagine…” Her eyes on Maria for a second, but there was no joy in it. Maria blinked, distracted for just a heartbeat, her mouth slightly agape as she quietly muttered, “Thanks…” You weren’t seeing any of it. It was all noise. Static. You were already moving, already acting. The gun felt like it had always belonged in your hand. The Thunderhead was all you could hear now, its voice as clear as a bell in your head, the target already set. (text-colour:#339af0)[**Terminate anti-federals.**] The rifle snapped into position. You didn’t need to hesitate. They didn’t even deserve your hesitation. The woman’s tear-streaked face blurred, her desperate eyes nothing more than distractions. The rifle clicked. Ready. The couple was nothing more than ghosts in the back of your mind now. Your finger tightened on the trigger. (text-colour:#ff6b6b)[**Terminate.**] You shot them.. You called it before the sound faded. **“Anti-Federals are Flatline.”** You’d done your job. The directive had been followed. **[[Leave The Apartment Room]]**The mission was over. You’d followed the orders, and now it was time to move on. You turned to leave. Your squad had done their job. It was clean. As you passed through the doorway, the grunt, a younger woman, was standing in the hallway, staring at the floor, her breath coming in shallow bursts. You barely noticed it at first, but then she tugged at your sleeve. You turned, feeling the frustration bubbling in your chest. "What is it now?" Her face was pale, eyes wide and desperate. "You.. you wouldn’t have done it. Not like that." You stepped back, confused. The grunt was shaking now. "They were civilians, Rowan. You said we weren’t supposed to..." She couldn't finish, as if she couldn't even believe what had just happened. "You wouldn’t have done it... You were different before." You stared at her, trying to process what she was saying. The Thunderhead's voice was loud in your mind, drowning out any hesitation. "They were linked to The Frost Shield," you said, your voice cold, almost automatic. "We’ve always hated them. They want to tear this empire down. They are enemies." You didn’t really believe what you were saying, not completely, but it was what you were supposed to say, what you needed to say to make it make sense. "We can’t afford to be weak." She didn’t respond at first. You could see the struggle in her eyes, like she was trying to hold herself together. But then she finally spoke again. "You wouldn’t have... You wouldn’t have killed them, Rowan. Not like this. Not just because you were told to. You’re better than this... You have a heart. You would have let someone else do it." The words hit harder than you expected. You knew what the mission demanded of you, what the Thunderhead commanded, but the grunt’s words made you question it, if only for a second. "This is nonsense. They’re the enemy. We’re leaving. Now." But she wouldn’t let it go. She tugged on your sleeve again, her grip firm now, though her voice was softer, almost pleading. "Please, Rowan... please, we can’t just walk away from this. Not like that." You were getting frustrated now, your patience wearing thin. You could feel the anger rising, the sharp edge of it cutting through your thoughts. "We have to go back! We’ve finished the job. If we stay here any longer, we’ll get punished. Both of us." But she just stood there, her eyes filled with confusion and sadness. "Whatever." she muttered, her voice low, as if she’d given up trying to change your mind. She turned away, but there was no relief in it. You didn’t understand what had just happened, didn’t understand why it felt like there was a crack in the foundation of your mind. But the mission was done. You had followed orders. There was no room for weakness, no room for doubt. You didn’t say anything else as you walked away. You couldn’t. There was nothing left to say. The grunt followed behind you, her footsteps soft, hesitant. **[[Ask Her About Rowan]]** **[[Question The Grunt]]** **[[Keep Walking.]]**The grunt was still trailing behind you, her footsteps quieter now. But as you moved, something was stuck at the back of your mind, something she had kept saying earlier. *Rowan* You stopped abruptly, causing her to almost bump into you. The word in your ears, louder with each passing second. It was a name, one you didn’t recognize, one that seemed to stick to you almost. “Why... why did you keep calling me *Rowan*?” Your voice was low, not harsh, but demanding. There was something inside you, some growing unease, that couldn’t let it go. The name *Rowan* didn’t feel like it belonged to you, and yet, somehow, it did. It wasn’t something you’d ever heard before, not in this life, at least. The Thunderhead’s influence clouded your memory, but you knew one thing: you’d never been called Rowan. The grunt didn’t answer immediately. She kept her eyes on the ground, shifting her look from one foot to the other, like she was waiting for something, or avoiding something. Finally, she spoke, but her voice was soft, barely audible. “It’s... it’s your name, isn’t it?” Her words sounded almost more like a question than a statement, as if she was unsure herself. You clenched your jaw, trying to keep the frustration from spilling out. "I don’t know what you’re talking about," you replied, more forceful. "My name is not Rowan. I don’t even know who that is." She looked up at you, confusion in her eyes. But then, just as quickly, her face hardened, like she was shutting something away. “If you don’t remember, then you don’t remember.” The response hit you like a cold slap. You felt a chill run through you, a deep, creeping. There was something there, something important that you couldn’t grasp, something that had slipped through your fingers.. **[["Who Am I To You?"]]** **[[Keep Walking.]]**As you both moved down the corridor, the sound of your boots the only noise as of right now. Her earlier breakdown, the way her hands shook and her voice faltered, kept replaying in your mind. You didn’t expect it from her, especially not someone who had expect to have seen it all before. You slowed your pace, turning your head just enough to catch her eye. "You alright?" The question was low, almost an afterthought, but you meant it. There was something raw about her back there, something cracked in her, something *human*. It didn’t sit right with you. Maybe it wasn’t supposed to. She didn’t answer immediately. Her eyes remained forward, looking through the hall, like she was swallowing something bitter. When she did speak, it was quiet, almost too quiet. “I’m fine.” but the tone gave it away. It wasn’t fine. Not by a long shot. You weren’t gonna get used to seeing grunts like this, so... human. And yet, it pulled at you, pulling you in. “You don’t look fine. I get it, though. Watching people die, it wears on the soul. Doesn’t it?” Her shoulders stiffened, but she didn’t turn to face you. You saw her hands ball into fists at her sides. “I don’t need a lecture from you.” You let out a breath, the words you wanted to say slipping out before you could stop them. “You know, once you get your card, things get easier. Stronger. Like me.” You said it almost absentmindedly, their ‘gifts,’ heavily on your shoulders. You’d been told it was normal to feel like this, that it was just part of the process. They said it was better to focus on the mission, focus on the strength they could offer. But the grunt... she wasn’t biting. She stopped walking for a brief moment, just enough to look at you. Her expression was tired, but there was something else there too. A knowing look that made your stomach tighten. “You think I want that?” she asked, voice dripping with sarcasm. “You think I’m gonna join the Federation’s army so I can be a soulless machine, just like you?” You stopped her, to counteract her.“It’s not about being soulless. It’s about making things better. Making the world safer. When you get your card, it’s not just about power. It’s about helping the Federation... it’s about helping everyone. It’s about being part of something bigger than yourself." She snorted, curling into a bitter smile. "Right. Something bigger." She stared at you like she already knew. "You really think that’s what they want? To make the world better? They don’t care about *us*, they don’t care about making the world better. They just want us to be their puppets. But hey, if I get stronger in the process... maybe it’ll be worth it." You could feel your frustration building again, pushing against the calm exterior you tried to maintain. "No, the Federation doesn’t want to control your soul. They want to *improve* it. Help us make things better. A safer world where people don’t have to live in fear. You know that." The grunt’s eyes narrowed, she twisted a cruel smile. "Is that what you tell yourself? I don’t know if I’m more disgusted or impressed that you can believe that. You really think this is all for the greater good? For the cause?" You looked at her for a long moment, the words stuck in your throat. Something in her voice, something in the way she said it made you question if you were just another puppet too. You were supposed to be fighting for a better world. But when you thought about it, when you really thought about it, it didn’t feel like that anymore. But instead of admitting it, you straightened up, pushing the uncomfortable thoughts aside. "What else is there? You think you’re better off fighting on your own? Out there? The Federation isn’t perfect, but it’s the only chance we’ve got." The grunt’s eyes softened for just a moment, vulnerability breaking through the tough exterior. “Maybe that’s the problem. Maybe we’re all just looking for a way to *survive*.” **[[Keep Walking.]]**The harsh wind from the city streets whipped against your face as you approached the entrance of the apartment building. It was still dark out, but not that you could notice with your constant red built in NVGs. As you neared the entrance, you could hear Sierra Team’s VTOL in the distance. The team was already regrouping, preparing to head back to base. They were silent, their usual banter replaced with the steely professionalism they had become known for. Your grunt companion, the one who had stuck by your side through the entire operation, was right behind you. You could sense the tiredness in them. But there was no time for rest. The team’s gear was already stowed, and the ramp was open, waiting for you to board. The grunt beside you gave you a brief nod, as if to say, *We made it through this. Let’s move.* The rest of Sierra Team was already onboard. One of the team leaders glanced your way, a silent acknowledgment in their eyes. It was over. You pushed through the door and into the VTOL. The ramp closed, sealing you inside. You took a seat, your grunt companion sitting next to you. The door slid shut, and the VTOL lifted off. The city below grew smaller as you ascended into the quiet of the sky. As the city lights blurred beneath you, a wave of relief washed over you. You could finally breathe, if only for a moment. Your grunt companion glanced at you once more, and this time, there was no need for words. As you lift off, your vision began to obstruct during the ride, as if you were falling asleep, but still awake at the same time. **[[THUNDERHEAD ITERATION.]]**“Who am I to you?” you asked, voice quieter now, though it still held an edge of suspicion. You could feel her distancing herself, but you needed to know. You had to understand. "What’s my name to you?" She didn’t answer right away, as though she was wrestling with her own thoughts. Then, after what felt like an eternity, she simply shook her head. “I... I don’t know what you’re talking about, Rowan.” The name sounded foreign coming from her, but there was something familiar about the way she said it. It felt like it should make sense, but it didn’t. It made your skin crawl, unsettled you in a way you couldn’t explain. "Why are you calling me that?" you pressed again, your voice slipping into something darker, the frustration boiling over. The grunt finally stopped walking, her eyes meeting your helmets cameras with an intensity you hadn’t expected. She took a deep breath, like she was about to say something important. But then her face softened, almost sadly, before she spoke. “I don’t know. I don’t know.” And with that, she fell silent again, her eyes falling to the floor as if she couldn’t bear to look at you. The rest of the world seemed to fall away in that moment, leaving you standing there with nothing but the pounding in your chest and the unanswered question still lingering between you. The doors were already open, the distant clatter of boots, the faint mix of voices, and the low mechanical sounds of the vehicles parked around the landing zone. Stepping out of the VTOL, you felt the ground firm beneath you, your body still a little stiff from the flight. No new orders came through as of yet, no new tasks to carry out. It was an odd feeling, standing there with no immediate purpose. But the grunt, was still nearby. She had her usual stoic expression, though there was a hint of something else in her eyes, something that hadn’t been there before. You caught her eye, and she met it with a small, almost imperceptible nod. She had something to say. You could tell. Before either of you could speak, two combative engineers approached swiftly, their movements synchronized as if they'd rehearsed it a hundred times before. Without hesitation, one of them stepped forward, lifting a scanner from his belt, he lifted up the grunts hair, revealing the barcode tattooed beneath. The second engineer activated the scanner, the soft *beep* as it scanned her ID. The grunt didn’t flinch. She had been through this a hundred times, no doubt. But you noticed her jaw tighten slightly as the engineers processed the scan. "You're coming with us. The commanding officer wishes to speak with you." The grunt’s eyes shifted toward you, a silent plea hidden behind her. She wasn’t exactly pleased with the sudden order, but there was no way to refuse. Not here. Not now. She reluctantly stepped with the engineers on either side, guiding her away from the landing pad. You watched as they escorted her toward the facility in the distance. Curiosity stirred inside you. Something didn’t sit right with you. You knew the grunt well enough by now to sense that she wasn’t just being called in for routine business. Something else was going on. Something more than just a simple debriefing. You hesitated for a moment, torn between respecting her space and the nagging feeling that you couldn’t just let this go. Without another thought, you made a split-second decision. You would follow them, but you’d need to act like you weren’t. You moved quietly, keeping a safe distance while making sure not to be noticed. You blended into the flow of soldiers moving around the facility, your steps calculated and purposeful. The engineers were focused on their task, but you could tell they were aware of their surroundings. You kept your posture neutral, not drawing attention to yourself as you followed them from behind, staying just out of sight. The two engineers led her through the door. You stayed by the doorway, just far enough to remain undetected, and watched them disappear inside. They had taken her to the commanding officer’s office. **[[Listen In The Conversation]]**You remained hidden just outside the door, your back pressed against the cold metal of the wall as you listened intently to the muffled voices inside. "The Thunderhead has reported your ID for attempting to corrupt federal soldiers, It's a common issue. You know how it is, we have no choice but to keep operations running." Another voice, one that seems to carry authority, spoke next. "We are going to have to terminate you. It's the only way to move forward. You caused deaths because of this. We are tired of it." Your heart sank. No consideration, no hesitation, just a cold, clinical decision to end a life that had only moments ago seemed like a insignificant thing to them. But to you, she wasn’t just some grunt. She was *her*. The one who had fought by your side, who had trusted you. You listened. You were trapped in the storm of the Thunderhead’s control, its influence pressing against your every thought, every impulse. *But…* Then it happened. You heard your name, your *real* name. "Rowan," you whispered to yourself, hearing it through the silence of your mind. "Rowan... Rowan." You repeated it a few more times, as if trying to anchor yourself to that single word, as if that word could remind you of who you really were. Your eyes widened, the fog of the Thunderhead’s influence cracking just enough to let something *human* bleed through. And then, just like that, the Thunderhead *activated*, its systems kicking into overdrive that immediately wanted to suppress any trace of defiance. (text-colour:#339af0)["Defiance detected."] the metallic voice of the Thunderhead inside your mind. (text-colour:#339af0)["You must comply. Reaffirm your loyalty."] But there was something different now, something you hadn’t expected. A loophole. You found it. You grasped it tightly, allowing it to spread through your consciousness like fire. The Thunderhead struggled, its grip on your mind slipping bit by bit as you pushed back against it. Your thoughts began to churn, harder and faster, as you fought to maintain control over your own will. *No* this was your mind. Your choice. You could feel the Thunderhead’s systems trying to force compliance, trying to fill your mind with its stale commands. But you were losing. It was too much, too fast. Your mind raced in confusion, a thousand thoughts overlapping each other as you tried to hold on to what little humanity remained inside you. And then you heard her voice again soft, but undeniable. "Rowan saved me you changed him! That's why I care!" *Yes...* That was right. You *had* saved her. You had done the impossible, and now, it was your turn to return the favor. You were *not* going to let her die. You couldn’t. The Thunderhead’s grip faltered. The system couldn’t calculate *this* couldn’t predict *you*. (text-colour:#c92a2a)[**[[REGAIN HUMANITY]]**]You unholstered your pulse rifle and stepped into the commander's office. The engineers, caught off-guard by your sudden entrance, barely had time to react. A quick shot from your rifle dropped them both before they could even draw a weapon. The two command officers looked up at you in shock, but it was too late. The crackling energy from the pulse rounds tore through them all. Maria’s eyes widened as she saw you, shock and gratitude flooding her face. But she didn’t speak a word. She didn’t have to. You walked over to her, adrenaline pumping through your veins. "Maria, I found myself." She didn’t say anything, just stepped forward and hugged you tightly, her arms wrapping around you in a brief, yet powerful embrace. For a moment, everything felt like it could be okay like there was still hope, a sense of purpose. But you knew better. The alarms blared to life, piercing the silence, and the unmistakable sound of boots marching down the corridor could already be heard. They knew something had happened. Quickly, you pulled away from her and looked around the room for options. There was no time. The sounds of the facility mobilizing around you were getting louder. You ran through the possibilities in your mind, fingers tapping against the pulse rifle in your hands as you thought through each escape route. There was no clear exit, but you would have to make one. **[[Pretend to be Injured]]** **[[Run Out]]**The alarms were deafening, but you couldn’t afford to let panic consume you. The sound of heavy boots down the hall as soldiers rushed into the office, their eyes scanning the room. The room was a mess, engineers and command officers laying dead on the floor, with you pretending to clutch your side in agony. You barely managed to get yourself into position, crumpling to the floor, wincing as if you had been struck during the firefight. Maria was beside you in an instant, her hand on your back, her voice low and urgent. "Stay with me.." The soldiers burst into the room, their weapons raised but lowering once they took in the scene. One of them quickly assessed the situation. “Bio signal lost. The commanding officer’s down… what happened here?” You gritted your teeth, forcing yourself to breathe heavily, clutching at your chest like you were barely holding on. You looked up at the federal soldiers. "The intruder... escaped. I was too... too late. They... got away." They paused, confusion across their faces. A few of them exchanged uncertain glances. They’d likely been expecting a fight, not this. You could see the doubt forming, but you had to sell this, had to make them believe the threat was gone. “Requesting medical support.” one soldier ordered into his comms, his voice tinged with urgency. Another soldier moved to help you, his hands gently pulling you into a sitting position. "You’ll be fine." he said, but you could tell he wasn’t sure. Maria, playing her part, spoke up as well, voice shaky but persuasive. "It... it was so fast. I don’t know what happened. He.. they.. came out of nowhere. Please... they need help." Another soldier nodded, motioning to the door. "Get the med team down here. We need to secure the area. The defunct may still be nearby." They all quickly turned and ran out of the office, leaving you and Maria alone for a brief moment. You exchanged a look. The deception had worked, for now. Maria nodded, glancing toward the exit. "What now?" They were going to be looking for the ‘intruder’ but you couldn’t stay here for long. But for the moment, they were on a different path. It was time to make your next move. **[[Head for the VTOL]]**The alarms blared as you and Maria hurried through the corridors of the facility. The VTOL pad was just ahead, its sleek silhouette faintly visible through the spotlights. The distant engines and the plethora of soldiers preparing to lock down the area filled the scene. You didn’t have much time. With a glance at Maria, you motioned for her to stay close. Her breathing heavy but controlled. The two of you darted through the shadows, running past open spaces and taking advantage of the chaos the alarms had created. Finally, you both reached the VTOL. The doors were still open, the cockpit’s systems blinking faintly, waiting for its next area. “Go!” you yelled at Maria, motioning for her to climb aboard. But as Maria scrambled into the VTOL, a shout came out behind you. “There! Unauthorized personnel near the VTOL!” You turned your head to see a squad of federal soldiers just rounding the corner, weapons raised. They didn’t hesitate, one of them went into his comms, “Attempting to leave unauthorized while under lockdown! Engaging!” Cursing under your breath, you grabbed Maria’s arm and pulled her fully inside the VTOL, slamming the door release. The hatch hissed as it began to close, but the soldiers were quick, already firing suppressing shots toward you. **[[Close the VTOL’s heavy door immediately and prepare for liftoff]]** **[[Grab the mounted pulse cannon from the side compartment]]** **[[Bluff your way out]]** **[[Escape on foot temporarily]]**<!-- Embed YouTube video background, hidden off-screen --> <iframe id="video-background" width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/a-X_9DsaHU8?autoplay=1&loop=1&playlist=a-X_9DsaHU8&mute=0&controls=0&showinfo=0&autohide=1" frameborder="0" allow="autoplay; fullscreen" style="position: absolute; left: -9999px; top: -9999px; z-index: 0; pointer-events: none;"></iframe> <!-- Death Screen Passage: YOU DIED! --> <div class="death-screen"> <h1 class="you-died-text">YOU DIED!</h1> <p class="quote-text">"You can’t outrun what’s already there, Idiot."</p> <div class="story-content"> <p>After the commanding officer hit the ground, his heart raced. The soldiers outside barely had time to react as the devastating burst of energy tears through them, leaving nothing but smoldering remnants. Their bodies drop, lifeless, as the VTOL's heavy door shuts. You quickly power up the engines and take to the skies, escaping the facility below. The tension in your chest slowly fades as the horizon stretches ahead. Maria, still catching her breath, glances at you with gratitude and awe. You’ve survived, for now. The VTOL soars through the air, steady as you leave the Federals behind. Canada waits, a cold, distant refuge, or a place where your troubles may only begin. You have to find a proper way to leave. Word has not gotten out yet, but be quick. His chest rose and fell with the slow rhythm of someone else’s machine, his breath measured and indifferent. The doctors stood nearby, their faces obscured by masks and visors, their voices an unintelligible of medical jargon. They didn’t acknowledge him beyond the occasional glance, and he didn’t care to interpret their words. Nothing mattered. The directive was all that remained.</p> <p>He stood from the hospital bed, the sterile white sheets falling away as he moved. The uniform of the Federation, gray and unfeeling, clung to him as though it were a second skin. His body felt like a stranger’s, every movement precise but hollow. The weight of the past, if it had ever existed, was gone. All that remained was the order. He did not question it. Questioning had no place in his mind anymore.</p> <p>The hallway stretched before him, featureless and unending, lined with the same sterile gray that enveloped his thoughts. His boots faintly against the metal floor, the sound quickly swallowed by the oppressive silence.</p> <p><em>Proceed to VTOL-2.</em> The directive burned quietly in his skull, clear and absolute. He moved without hesitation, his body following the order as if it had always known the way. The Federation insignia emblazoned on his chest glinted under the cold fluorescent lights.</p> <p>Rowan passed others in the hallway. Some were soldiers, their faces hidden behind helmets, indistinguishable from one another. Others were technicians, their eyes flicking toward him briefly before returning to their consoles. No one spoke. No one stopped him. He didn’t look at them; they were irrelevant. He had his orders.</p> <p>The transport bay was just ahead, its large doors sliding open with a hiss of pressurized air as he approached. Inside, the VTOL sat waiting, its sleek look illuminated by the harsh lights of the open liftoff point.</p> <p>Rowan stepped onto the platform. A group of soldiers were already inside, their helmets in place, their postures rigid. None of them turned to acknowledge him. They were like him, silent, obedient. He walked past them without a word, his eyes fixed on the seat assigned to him.</p> <p>As he reached his station, his eyes was fixed on the helmet waiting there. Smooth and impersonal, it was more than just armor; it was the final piece of the Federation’s grip on him. The moment it sealed over his head, there would be nothing left of Rowan, nothing to separate him from the others. It would quiet the faint awareness still buried deep within him, smothering it beneath layers of control and compliance.</p> <p>He lifted the helmet, its weight both familiar and alien in his hands as he lowered it over his head, the world narrowing into a field of data overlays and tactical readouts.</p> <p>Rowan no longer existed. The directive was all that mattered now.</p> <p>Without a second thought, he strapped into his seat. The VTOL’s engines came to life, the vibrations coursing through the cabin as the craft prepared for takeoff. Outside the small window, the hangar blurred into motion as the VTOL lifted off the ground, carrying him and the others toward their next objective. Whatever it was, he did not question it. He did not think about it. Thinking was unnecessary.</p> <p>He stared ahead, his vision filled with the cold glow of tactical data. The directive hummed steadily in his mind, a constant companion in the void of his thoughts. The Federation’s voice was the only voice now. The heavy hum of the turbines began to dull as the craft’s engines powered down, and the ramp at the rear of the vehicle slid open with a hiss. Rowan’s vision, which had been clouded for the entire ride, cleared in an instant as the technology embedded into his helmet deactivated. The world around him snapped into focus, detailed, and full of purpose. He blinked, adjusting to the sudden view. The squad began to move as one, their boots hitting the ground. The Sergeant, a tall man with a square jaw and a demeanor that matched the weight of his rank, stood still for a moment. He listened intently to his comms, the faint static of the overwatch chatter filling his earpiece. His eyes narrowed slightly as he processed the incoming feed. Rowan felt a hand at his side, pulling out the pulse rifle that had been secured to his combat harness. It was lighter than expected, a deadly weapon with a metallic sheen. He'd been given a genetic code, encoded directly into his DNA, which unlocked the weapon's security features. The rifle was now his, responding only to his touch. Outside, the night stretched endlessly, peppered with faint stars. Snow flurries danced through the darkness, brushing against the glass like whispers of winter. A faint warning chime filled the cabin, drawing his groggy attention to the console. **Landing Zone Unsafe. Recommend Redirection Verdict.** He frowned, rubbing his eyes as the console lights cast an amber glow across the cockpit. "Damn it," he muttered under his breath, adjusting his seat. The snowy expanse of British Columbia loomed below, its everwhite forests shimmering faintly under the moonlight. “You’re awake.” Rowan turned his head. Clara, seated beside him, her sharp eyes scanning the screen. “I know this province,” she said evenly. “I know someone who can help us..” Her tone caught Rowan off guard. He raised a brow, the tension easing from his shoulders slightly. “Help us? You sure?” Clara nodded firmly. “There’s an underground group. Rebels. I know where they are.” Rowan leaned forward, setting the VTOL to hover as he considered her words. “Coordinates?” he asked. She pointed to a location deeper into the wilderness, far from any settlements. “Here.” Rowan input the coordinates, glancing at her sidelong. “How do you know about this?” Clara didn’t answer immediately, her eyes fixed on the snow-covered landscape outside. “It’s better if you don’t ask.” Rowan narrowed his eyes, but something in her tone made him stop pressing. Instead, he nodded and adjusted the VTOL’s course. “Alright. If you say they’ll help…” “They will,” Clara cut him off, her voice quiet but certain. As they neared the coordinates, the VTOL’s console beeped again. Rowan guided the craft lower, scanning for a place to land. A clearing appeared, surrounded by towering pines. It would have to do. The landing was rough, the VTOL’s skids sinking into the snow with a muffled crunch. Rowan powered down the engines, the hum fading into the stillness of the forest. He unstrapped himself and grabbed his rifle, slinging it over his shoulder as he stood. Clara was already waiting at the hatch, her silhouette framed by the icy moonlight. The forest was eerily quiet, save for the crunch of snow beneath their boots and the occasional gust of wind that whispered through the towering pines. Rowan followed Clara, his unease growing with every step. Her confidence unsettled him, this wasn’t the aimless wandering of someone following vague directions. She knew exactly where she was going. “Clara,” Rowan called. “How do you know where this place is?” Clara didn’t slow her pace. “I told you, I know someone here,” she replied, her tone clipped. “That’s not good enough,” Rowan said, quickening his stride to catch up. “We’re talking about a hidden rebel base in Federation territory. Places like this don’t just show up on a map. So, how do you know?” She glanced at him briefly, her expression unreadable in the dim moonlight. “You’ll get your answers when we get there.” “Not good enough,” Rowan muttered under his breath, gripping the strap of his rifle tightly. For a moment, Clara said nothing, her boots crunching through the snow. Then she stopped abruptly at the edge of a ridge, gesturing to the shadows below. “There.” Rowan followed her eyes, his own narrowing. Nested against the slope was a steel door, partially buried under layers of snow and earth. It was massive and reinforced, blending seamlessly into the landscape. “That’s it?” he asked, his skepticism clear. “That’s it,” Clara confirmed. She turned to him, her expression suddenly serious. “Knock.” Rowan hesitated, his eyes going between her and the door. “Why don’t you knock? You’re the one who—” “Just do it,” Clara snapped, her voice sharp enough to cut through his hesitation. “Please.” Rowan sighed, stepping toward the door. Its surface was cold under his gloved hand as he pounded on it. The sound echoed through the still night, sending faint vibrations up his arm. For a moment, there was nothing. Then a gruff voice called out, muffled by the thick steel. “Who is here?” Rowan froze, unsure of what to say. He turned to Clara, but she was already stepping closer, her breath visible in the freezing air. “Say this,” she whispered urgently, leaning in. “*Shadow of the flame, born of the void.*” Rowan frowned, his unease growing. “What does that mean?” “Just say it,” she insisted, her eyes locking with his. “Trust me.” He hesitated but eventually turned back to the door, his voice steady. “Shadow of the flame, born of the void.” There was a long pause. Then the voice barked again. “Step back from the door.” Rowan did as he was told, retreating a few paces. Clara stayed where she was, her eyes fixed on the door as a low hum began to emanate from within. Slowly, the door groaned, sliding open with a hiss of hydraulics. What greeted them on the other side wasn’t an open invitation. Armed rebels poured out, their weapons trained on Rowan, AR-15s interspersed and others armed with sleek Federal pulse rifles. Rowan’s heart raced as he instinctively raised his hands. His eyes darted to the pulse rifles, their sleek designs unmistakable. “How the hell are they using those?” he muttered. The rifles were bio-locked to Federation soldiers, rendering them useless to anyone else. The rebels didn’t answer his unspoken question. A tall man with a scar running down his cheek stepped forward, his rifle aimed squarely at Rowan’s chest. “Who the hell are you, and how did you find this place?” Rowan hesitated, his pulse pounding in his ears. “Her,” he said, nodding toward Clara. “She led me here.” The man’s brow furrowed as he glanced around. “Who?” Rowan turned toward Clara, his confusion mounting. “Her,” he repeated, pointing directly at her. “The woman standing right there. Clara.” The rebels exchanged uneasy glances, their weapons shifting slightly. “There’s no one there,” one of them muttered. “What are you talking about?” Rowan snapped, his voice rising. “She’s right—” His words faltered as he turned fully to Clara. She was still there, but something had changed. Her shoulders were hunched, and her face was streaked with tears that glistened in the moonlight. “Clara,” Rowan said cautiously, stepping toward her. “Why are you crying?” She didn’t answer. Her lips trembled as she hugged herself tightly, her entire frame shaking. The scarred man’s eyes narrowed, a face of recognition crossing his face. “Take him inside,” he yelled, his voice sharp. Two rebels moved quickly, grabbing Rowan by the arms. He tried to shake them off, his panic rising. “Hey! What’s going on? What’s wrong with her?” He glanced back at Clara, but she remained motionless, her tears falling silently. The scarred man leaned in close, his voice low and grim. “You’ve got no idea what you’ve brought here, do you?” Rowan’s protests fell on deaf ears as they dragged him toward the facility. The massive doors groaned shut behind them, the sound echoing ominously in the confined space. As they hauled him deeper into the rebel stronghold, Rowan’s mind raced. Who was Clara? What had he stumbled into? And why, when he looked back at her in those final moments, did she seem less human and more like a shadow of something far darker? **[[Dream..]]**<!DOCTYPE html> <html lang="en"> <head> <meta charset="UTF-8"> <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"> <title>THUNDERHEAD Iteration</title> <style> body { margin: 0; padding: 0; background: linear-gradient(180deg, #00141a, #000814); color: #ffffff; font-family: "Orbitron", sans-serif; height: 200vh; overflow-y: auto; } @keyframes glow { 0% { text-shadow: 0 0 10px #00f, 0 0 20px #0ff, 0 0 30px #0ff; } 50% { text-shadow: 0 0 15px #00f, 0 0 30px #0ff, 0 0 45px #0ff; } 100% { text-shadow: 0 0 10px #00f, 0 0 20px #0ff, 0 0 30px #0ff; } } .content { max-width: 90%; margin: 50px auto; padding: 40px; background: rgba(0, 0, 30, 0.85); border-radius: 10px; box-shadow: 0 0 40px rgba(0, 255, 255, 0.3); backdrop-filter: blur(5px); overflow: hidden; } .section { margin-bottom: 30px; } .left { color: #00ffff; animation: glow 2s infinite; } .right { color: #aaa; } .highlight { color: #ff66ff; font-style: italic; } .ellipsis { font-size: 2rem; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 10px; color: #aaa; } /* Hidden YouTube video */ .hidden-video { position: fixed; top: -100px; left: -100px; width: 1px; height: 1px; opacity: 0; pointer-events: none; } </style> </head> <body> <!-- Hidden YouTube video --> <iframe class="hidden-video" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/obo9lB6rNr0?autoplay=1&mute=0&loop=1&playlist=obo9lB6rNr0" frameborder="0" allow="autoplay" allowfullscreen> </iframe> <div class="content"> <div class="section"> <p class="left">[AWAKE. His body felt heavy, his mind still groggy from the remnants of his dreams, half memories, half fleeting specters of war. A gentle shake on his shoulder interrupted the stillness. “Hey, sleepyhead,” came Maria’s voice, warm and teasing. Her tone carried a hint of exasperation but mostly affection. “You planning on sleeping through the apocalypse, or what?” Rowan groaned, burying his face deeper into the pillow. “Five more minutes…” “Nope!” Maria said firmly, her grin audible. “Not on my watch.” She gave his shoulder another shake before stepping back, crossing her arms as she watched him stir. Reluctantly, Rowan turned over, his hazel eyes squinting up at her as the sunlight caught her figure. She looked impossibly put-together for this early in the morning, her short hair catching the light, her expression equal parts soft and determined. “Fine, fine.” Rowan muttered, sitting up and rubbing his face. “You’re relentless, you know that?” Maria smirked, leaning down to meet his eye level. “And you’re predictable. Now come on, your mom’s cooked up something amazing, and you don’t want to miss it.” The aroma of sizzling bacon and sweet maple syrup wafted through the air as Rowan trudged down the stairs with Maria close behind. The kitchen was alive with energy. His mom was at the stove, flipping pancakes onto a growing stack, Nessa was already sneaking a bite of toast from the table. “Good morning, honey!” his mom called out cheerily, glancing over her shoulder. “Go on, take a seat. Breakfast is ready.” Rowan slipped into a chair beside Maria, who wasted no time grabbing a plate. Across from them, Nessa leaned forward, her eyes bright with curiosity. “Alright, everyone, dig in!” his dad declared, setting down his coffee mug with a satisfied sigh. The table clattered with the sound of plates being passed around, forks scraping, and idle chatter. Rowan had barely taken a bite of the warm, buttery pancakes before Nessa pounced. “So, Rowan,” she began, her voice cutting through the morning din, “the cyberware lining… did they really change you?” Rowan stiffened slightly, glancing at Maria. Her expression was neutral, but the slight shift of her hand brushing against his under the table was grounding. He took a deep breath. “Yeah,” he admitted. “They did. It’s standard for soldiers. They don’t really give us a choice.” Nessa’s eyes widened. “Whoa. Like… what kind of stuff? Super strength? Laser eyes?” Rowan couldn’t help but chuckle softly, though his smile didn’t quite reach his eyes. “Not exactly. They installed a neural implant. It enhances reflexes, reaction times, stuff like that. They gave me synthetic muscles and whatever.. I think.. I don't know.” Nessa tilted her head. “That doesn’t sound too bad. But you look… weird about it. Is there something else?” Rowan hesitated, the fork in his hand hovering over his plate. “The implant… it’s not just enhancements. It’s invasive. Sometimes it tries to… take over. Like, push me out of my own head.” The room grew uncomfortably quiet. Even the sounds of forks and knives scraping against plates stopped. His dad set his coffee cup down, his expression darkening. “Take over? What the hell does that mean?” Rowan swallowed hard. “It’s hard to explain. The implant… it amplifies certain instincts, certain thoughts. Makes you more… compliant. At least, that’s what it’s supposed to do.” His mom looked stricken. “But you’re okay now, right? You said it almost took over. How did you stop it?” Rowan finally looked up, his gaze meeting Maria’s. “Maria. She… she kept me grounded. Pulled me back when I was slipping. If it weren’t for her, I’m not sure I’d still be… me.” Maria’s cheeks flushed slightly under the weight of everyone’s attention, but she shrugged, trying to downplay it. “It wasn’t a big deal. Just… doing what anyone would do.” Rowan’s dad frowned, leaning back in his chair. “I always thought Thunderhead, the stuff they show on TV, was supposed to help soldiers keep their minds together. Guess they left out the part where they put your minds at risk in the first place.” Rowan nodded grimly. “Yeah. They’re good at telling people what they want to hear. But now you know the truth.” Sensing the heaviness of the moment, his mom cleared her throat and smiled at Maria. “Well, Maria, you’ve been a lifesaver in more ways than one, it seems. Tell us more about yourself, dear.” Maria blinked, caught off guard. “Oh, uh, what do you want to know?” Rowan’s dad leaned forward, a mischievous glint in his eye. “Are you two… y’know… an item? You know, doing soldier stuff.” His dad leaned forward, pretending to think seriously. “Doing soldier stuff, huh? I can only imagine… maybe you swept her off her feet, like some sort of big heroic moment? Maybe you had to fight off *super* soldiers in an alleyway somewhere? Or maybe you two locked eyes across a crowded room, she was wearing a red dress and you just knew she was the one.” Rowan groaned, his face turning bright red. “Come on, Dad, you’re getting way ahead of yourself.” He shot Maria a look, and she was laughing now, her eyes twinkling. “Well, what *really* happened then?” his mom asked, leaning forward slightly. “I’d love to hear the *real* story.” Rowan sighed, feeling a bit cornered. “Well, I saved her from some skeeter boys, but not in the way Dad imagines. It then all started with… a conversation. A few awkward exchanges, but we started talking more and more, and before long… we got closer.” His mom raised an eyebrow, but before she could respond, his dad cut in again, now genuinely curious but trying to hide it behind his usual teasing tone. “Ah, so you two *grew closer*, huh? Is that how you’d describe it?” Rowan chuckled nervously, tapping his fingers on the table. “Well, yeah. But it wasn’t all smooth sailing. At one point, I thought it’d be a good idea to take a *top-up* you know, that boost that soldiers sometimes get to make them stronger. Thought it would make me more powerful, you know, so I could be more… well, useful.” His dad raised his eyebrows. “Stronger, huh? And did it work?” Rowan sighed, leaning back in his chair, thinking for a moment. “Yeah, it worked. But it wasn’t all good. At first, it just made me *mindless*, like I was losing myself. I don’t really know how to explain it. The more I took it, the more I felt like I was becoming… someone else. Someone who didn’t really care, someone who didn’t think about anything but power.” Maria’s expression softened, the playful teasing momentarily fading. “But Rowan, you came through it. You didn’t lose yourself. I was there with you when it happened. I don’t know how, but you *fought* it. You came back.” Rowan nodded, feeling a lump in his throat. “Yeah. It wasn’t easy, but I had to. It was either that or… lose everything. And, well… it wasn’t just about the power. It was about *me*.” The table was quiet for a moment, everyone digesting what Rowan had just shared. His mom broke the silence, her tone a little softer now. “I’m glad you were able to pull through, Rowan. That’s not something easy to face.” Rowan shrugged, a small smile tugging at his lips. “I had some help. Maria was there when I needed her most.” His dad smiled knowingly, though he didn’t press the issue. “Well, sounds like we’ve got a pretty strong bond here, huh?” he said, glancing between them both. “Just don’t expect us to stop asking questions anytime soon.” Maria’s eyes sparkled with amusement. “Wouldn’t dream of it.” Rowan’s dad grinned, nudging his wife. “You know, Maria’s a real looker. Where’d you get that from?” Maria laughed, her cheeks flushing slightly at the compliment. “From my mom, I guess. She’s got the looks, but I got the charm.” Rowan’s mom smiled at her daughter’s compliment, her eyes softening. “Well, I can see it. You’re a lovely girl, Maria. We’re glad to have you around.” Maria smiled warmly at her. “Thanks. I’m glad to be here.” The conversation shifted back to more casual topics, but the playful teasing about Rowan and Maria was still around. Rowan felt a strange sense of comfort, despite the teasing, his family cared, and that meant a lot. As the table finally began to empty, with everyone finishing their breakfast, Nessa leaned back in her chair, looking between Rowan and Maria with a smirk. “Well, I guess we’ll just have to keep guessing for now, huh?” Rowan rolled his eyes but couldn’t suppress the smile. “You can keep guessing all you want, but nothing’s set in stone yet.” Maria, glancing at Rowan, nodded thoughtfully. “Yeah… nothing’s decided just yet. But I’m *definitely* sticking around.” *knock knock knock* There was someone at the door, this early in the morning? **[[Who's There..]]**Maria’s laughter tapered off, but the amused glint in her eyes didn’t fade. She leaned back in her chair, crossing her arms as she gave Rowan a sideways glance. “Well, Rowan,” she said playfully, “are you going to answer your dad, or should I?” Rowan rubbed the back of his neck, his cheeks flushed. “Alright, alright,” he muttered, trying to summon some courage. “Yeah. Maria’s my girlfriend.” His mom clasped her hands together, her face lighting up. “Oh, Rowan! That’s wonderful!” Rowan’s dad chuckled, leaning back with a triumphant grin. “Knew it. You don’t bring someone to family breakfast unless it’s serious.” Maria raised an eyebrow at Rowan, her smirk growing. “Serious, huh?” she teased, her tone light but not dismissive. “Yeah. It is.” Rowan paused, his voice softening. “Maria’s… she’s not just my girlfriend. She’s been with me through everything. When I didn’t even know if I could keep going, she was there. She’s—” He stopped, realizing how much he was spilling. “Well, she’s important to me. Really important.” Maria’s teasing demeanor fell slightly, replaced by something warmer, softer. “You’re important to me too, Rowan,” she said quietly, her voice steady but full of emotion. “Didn’t think I’d ever see it,” James quipped, shaking his head in mock disbelief. “Maria, you’re a miracle worker.” Rowan rolled his eyes but couldn’t hide the small smile tugging at his lips. His mom reached across the table to squeeze his hand, her own eyes shimmering with pride. “I’m so glad you’ve found someone like Maria, Rowan. She’s clearly good for you.” The table erupted into laughter. His family’s acceptance and Maria’s presence grounding him in a way he hadn’t felt in years. For the first time in a long time, he let himself believe that maybe, just maybe, things could be okay. *knock knock knock* There was someone at the door, this early in the morning? **[[Who's There..]]**Rowan shifted uncomfortably in his chair, rubbing the back of his neck. He hadn’t expected his dad to ask such a direct question, and for a second, he found himself fumbling for words. He stole a quick glance at Maria, who gave him a knowing look, her face twitching into a small smile. “Uh…” Rowan began, his voice slightly strained, “Yeah, I guess... Maria’s my girlfriend.” He paused, unsure how to continue, but Maria’s calm presence beside him helped him push forward. “It’s still... new, I guess. But, yeah, it’s serious in its own way.” He shrugged, trying to downplay the his words but also not hide how much it meant. Maria tilted her head, her smile softening. “It’s not perfect, but it’s real,” she added, her voice steady. “We’ve been through a lot, and yeah, we’re still figuring things out. But we’re here. And that counts for something.” His dad raised an eyebrow, clearly amused but not dismissive. “That’s a fair answer, son. I can respect that.” He leaned back in his chair, hands clasped behind his head. “It’s good to see you’re not jumping into something you’re not ready for.” Rowan nodded, relieved his dad wasn’t pushing him further. “Yeah. I’m not one to rush into things, especially with everything going on. But she’s... she’s important to me. More than I thought anyone would be, honestly.” Maria’s smile softened, her fingers brushing lightly against his under the table. “Same here,” she said quietly, giving him a small, reassuring squeeze. Nessa leaned forward, propping her chin on her hand with a mischievous grin. “So, you’re telling me you’re not *officially* dating, but you’re basically already a couple?” Rowan laughed awkwardly, looking at Maria. “Yeah, something like that,” he admitted. “It’s complicated, but... yeah, that’s the gist of it. Considering we escaped a murderous empire, yeah.” Maria chuckled, her tone teasing. “You’re so bad at this,” she teased Rowan gently, earning a mock glare from him. “Hey, I’m trying,” he shot back, a grin tugging at the corners of his mouth. “You’re the one who keeps me on my toes.” His mom smiled fondly at the two of them, though there was a trace of concern in her expression. “I’m just happy to see you both making the effort. It’s not always easy, but if you’re both giving it a shot, then I’m behind you.” “Thanks, Mom,” Rowan said, feeling her approval in a way he didn’t quite know how to respond to. Maria gave his hand a final squeeze before taking a bite of her toast. “It’s definitely a work in progress,” she said with a smile, her eyes locking with Rowan’s, “but I’m all in.” Rowan nodded, the uncertainty still there but not as overwhelming as before. “Yeah... me too.” He leaned back in his chair, feeling the warmth of the moment, complicated, uncertain, but somehow perfect. *knock knock knock* There was someone at the door, this early in the morning? **[[Who's There..]]**Nessa immediately stood up, wiping her hands on her apron as she made her way toward the door, her face lighting up with a smile, eager to see who it could be. But as her fingers wrapped around the cold metal handle, a sudden unease swept over her, a knot tightening in her stomach. The moment she opened the door, that feeling hit her like a wave. Standing there were the unmistakable figures of the Federation. A tall, stern-looking SIA agent with his high-tech mono goggles glinting in the morning light, a federal officer wearing a plain, gray uniform, and two federal soldiers flanking his sides, their weapons holstered but their presence still heavy with authority. The officer was the one who spoke first, his voice somber, his eyes scanning the room with an almost rehearsed sadness. “Good morning. I’m afraid I have some difficult news.” the officer said, his tone soft but unyielding. “Rowan Whitlock, your son... He won’t be coming home.” Nessa’s heart dropped into her stomach. The words felt like they were crushing her from the inside out, but she couldn’t show it. She had to hold it together. She had to protect Rowan. The officer continued, his voice feigning sorrow, but his eyes betrayed him. “It is with a heavy heart that I inform you that your son died while on duty. His actions... they were dishonorable. He betrayed the Federation. And for that, he will not be returning.” Rowan’s dad stiffened. His face turned ashen, his hand gripping the edge of the doorframe as he looked at the officer, his knuckles whitening. “What do you mean ‘betrayed the Federation’?” His voice was barely a whisper, but there was a fire behind it. “You’re telling me my son... *my* son died like that? You’re lying.” The officer’s face remained neutral, but he lowered his voice just slightly, the hint of insincerity still there. “I’m sorry for your loss. The Federation offers its condolences. We’ll make sure that all his affairs are settled accordingly.” He glanced at the two soldiers beside him, who stood at attention, probably not even blinking. Nessa, her hands trembling, quickly stepped into the doorway, blocking the officer’s view into the house. “You’re wrong. He’s not dead. My son is not dead,” she said through clenched teeth, her voice barely above a whisper. She swallowed hard, trying to maintain her composure. “You’re lying, and I’m not going to let you take him away.” It was happening. They had no time to waste. Rowan moved first, his feet silent against the floor as he stepped toward the back door, signaling Maria to follow. The officer was distracted, busy speaking his rehearsed lines to Nessa, and this gave them the moment they needed. They moved quickly, slipping into the hallway and then through the kitchen. Maria grabbed Rowan’s arm, whispering fiercely under her breath. “We need to hide. Now.” Rowan nodded, his heart pounding in his chest. He could feel the cold weight of the officer’s lies creeping into his bones, but he couldn’t stop now. They had to make sure his family was safe, even if it meant disappearing for a while. They ducked into the basement, where they had hidden things before, a small, quiet space that no one could easily access. Meanwhile, back at the door, the officer gave his speech, his voice dripping with faux sorrow. “Your son’s actions were dishonorable. We had hoped he’d return to serve the Federation, but we see now that was not to be. We’ll be processing the information and securing his file.” He bowed his head slightly, as if to feign a final gesture of respect, though it was clear it was all a performance. “We deeply regret his decision, and we’ll make sure to address it.” But before Nessa could respond, before she could say anything else, she heard a low, mechanical whirring noise. The SIA agent’s mono-goggle activated, the single iris of his one goggle flickering with a sharp purple light. He tilted his head slightly, then looked up, his gaze locking onto Nessa. There was a cold, calculating edge to his stare. “Lies,” he said, the single word carrying, like a knife cutting through the officer’s words. “We know your son is still alive.” The air seemed to freeze in that moment. Nessa’s stomach churned. How could he know? How much had they seen? Her mind raced. The SIA agent continued, his voice robotic, devoid of any compassion. “They had a VTOL. It landed near this general area. You wouldn’t be trying to hide your son from us, would you?” His eye never left as he took a step forward, and Nessa instinctively took a step back, her heart pounding in her chest. “I—I don’t know what you’re talking about.” she stammered, trying to keep her voice steady. “My son is dead. There’s nothing to hide. He’s not here. You can search if you need to, but you won’t find anything.” The officer glanced at the SIA agent, who nodded subtly, and then he turned back to Nessa, a thin smile tugging at the corners of his lips. “We’ll be searching your house to make sure everything is in order. It’s just a formality.” His voice remained smooth, but there was an unmistakable contrast beneath it now, a pressure that only grew stronger with each passing moment. Nessa knew they didn’t have much time. The SIA agent’s presence alone meant they were already onto something. He was relentless, and once he started searching, there was no telling how long it would take before they found what they were looking for. They were getting closer to discovering the truth. As the SIA agent moved forward, Nessa’s mind spun. If they searched the house and found anything, anything out of place, it would be all over. They had to be careful, had to think fast. "Go ahead," Nessa said, her voice trembling as she wiped away an imaginary tear. She forced a sob to her, hoping it would make her seem more convincing. "He's not here. You’ve got the wrong place. My son is dead. You’ve already told us that." The SIA agent’s goggles flared again as he scanned the room. His movements were swift, methodical. The room was silent except for the faint buzz of his equipment. The agent’s eye looked toward the stairs that led down to the basement. He hesitated, just for a moment, as if looking at his next move. His instincts told him something was off. With the soldiers watching from behind, the SIA agent moved toward the stairs, his boots making no sound against the floor as he descended. "Wait," Nessa said, her voice shaky. "He's... he's not here. I swear." She forced herself to sound distraught, wiping away another tear. “You can search, but you won’t find him.” The agent paused, his head tilting slightly. His eyes never left her. He wasn’t convinced. He knew something was up. He always did. He signaled for the soldiers to follow. They began their search, and Nessa could feel the seconds stretching into eternity as they moved through the house. The SIA agent paused at the base of the stairs, their head tilting ever so slightly. The flicking of their mono-goggle was a mechanical twitch that made Nessa’s stomach churn. They kept their eyes on her, as if peeling back every layer of her composure, seeking the truth she desperately tried to conceal. “You’re hiding something.” the agent said. Without waiting for a reply, they signaled to the soldiers. “Search the premises. Top to bottom.” The soldiers moved, their heavy boots thudding against the wooden floor. Nessa stood frozen in the living room, her eyes darting toward the basement door, praying it would hold just a little longer. Rowan and Maria were down there, hiding, holding their breaths. Every creak of the floorboards above felt like a death knell. The agent’s mono-goggle flicked again, scanning the house as they ascended the stairs. They moved with an unnatural quietness, their presence as oppressive as the void. Nessa’s voice waved as she followed them. “Please, we have nothing to hide. My family… we’ve done nothing wrong. He’s gone. There’s nothing here.” The agent ignored her completely, their focus narrowing as they approached the master bedroom. Pushing the door open, their gaze immediately fixed on a sleek black object leaning against the corner of the room: a pulse rifle. Its design was unmistakably Federation-issue. The agent’s gloved hand reached out, gripping the weapon as their mono-goggle scanned its serial number. A match. It was Rowans rifle. The rifle hummed faintly in their grasp, the energy within it barely contained. Downstairs, Rowan and Maria’s hearts pounded in unison. The muffled movements above were growing louder. Rowan clenched his jaw, his eyes darting to the basement’s back door. He whispered urgently, “We have to go. Now.” Maria hesitated, her face pale, but she nodded. Together, they crept toward the door, their steps as silent as they could manage. Above them, the SIA agent descended the stairs, the pulse rifle now in their hands. Nessa’s pleas became frantic. “Please! That’s not ours! We’ve never seen it before! You have to believe me!” The agent didn’t even look at her. Their voice was devoid of emotion. “Illegal possession of federal firearms. 3.2 infraction confirmed.” They turned to the officer standing by the doorway. “Secure the suspects.” The officer hesitated, glancing at Nessa and her husband. His expression was inhuman, almost reluctant. “You heard them,” he yelled to the soldiers. “Move!” At that moment, Rowan and Maria burst through the basement door, sprinting into the snow-covered field behind the house. The commotion drew everyone’s attention. “Two suspects fleeing!” one soldier shouted, immediately giving chase. The SIA agent’s head snapped toward the fleeing figures. They signaled to the remaining soldiers. “Secure the premises. Eliminate any resistance.” Nessa’s husband stepped forward, desperation in his voice. “Wait! You don’t understand. We—” The officer raised a hand, cutting him off. His eyes were cold as he gestured to one of the soldiers. The unspoken command was clear. Nessa’s sobs filled the room as the soldier’s weapon was raised. The doors closed, muffling the sound of the shots that followed. When the officer stepped outside moments later, his expression betrayed no emotion, but the faint smear of blood on his boot spoke volumes. Meanwhile, Rowan and Maria ran as fast as their legs could carry them, the icy air burning their lungs. But they weren’t fast enough. A soldier tackled Rowan to the ground, the impact knocking the wind out of him. Maria screamed, struggling as another soldier grabbed her, pinning her arms behind her back. Rowan thrashed, his voice raw with anguish. “Let her go! Let her go!” The officer arrived moments later, brushing snow off his uniform. He surveyed the scene with a faint smirk, pulling out his communicator. “Targets apprehended. VTOL en route.” The SIA agent emerged from the house, the pulse rifle still in their grip. Their mono-goggle flickered as they scanned Rowan and Maria, lingering on Rowan’s tear-streaked face. “You’ll answer for your crimes,” they said, their voice icy. “The Federation does not tolerate traitors.” The sound of the approaching VTOL grew louder, its engines slicing through the silence. The soldiers forced Rowan and Maria to their feet, injecting them with nanobiotics to subdue them. As the serum coursed through their veins, their struggles slowed, and their vision blurred.
