[[ Sleep ]]<!DOCTYPE html> <html lang="en"> <head> <meta charset="UTF-8"> <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"> <title>Rowan's Dream</title> <style> body { margin: 0; padding: 0; font-family: "Merriweather", serif; background: radial-gradient(circle, #0c0c0c 60%, #070707 100%); color: #d1d1d1; line-height: 1.8; text-align: center; padding: 50px 20px; } .dream { max-width: 800px; margin: 0 auto; } .section { margin-bottom: 80px; } .peaceful { font-size: 1.6rem; color: #a8d3ff; } .shift { font-size: 1.5rem; color: #f8c471; } .ominous { font-size: 1.6rem; color: #f39c12; } .nightmare { font-size: 1.8rem; color: #ff7171; } .dark { font-size: 2rem; color: #d14141; font-weight: bold; } iframe.hidden-audio { position: fixed; bottom: -10px; right: -10px; width: 1px; height: 1px; opacity: 0; } </style> </head> <body> <div class="dream"> <div class="section peaceful"> The air was warm, the sun casting a golden glow over an endless meadow. Rowan walked barefoot, feeling the soft tickle of grass between his toes. A river glittered nearby, its waters so clear he could see the pebbles at its bottom, each stone a different vibrant color. He could hear the gentle rush of the current, a sound that soothed his weary soul. Birds sang overhead, their melodies intertwining in perfect harmony. In the distance stood a house, simple yet inviting, smoke curling from its chimney. As he approached, the front door opened, and a figure stepped out, a beautiful woman with kind eyes and a radiant smile. She waved at him. "Welcome home." she said, her voice like the melody of the birds. </div> <div class="section shift"> Inside the house, a warm fire cracked in the hearth. A table was set, laden with food, fresh bread, ripe fruit, and a steaming stew. The woman guided Rowan to a chair, her touch light yet reassuring. "You’ve been through so much," she said. "It’s time to rest." Rowan took a bite of the bread, its flavor richer than anything he had ever tasted. But as he chewed, he noticed the room dimming. The fire flickered, its once warm light now casting shadows that twisted unnaturally. He looked at the woman, but her kind eyes were now dark pits, her smile stretching unnaturally wide. "Rest," she repeated, her voice distorted, like a hollow wind. </div> <div class="section ominous"> Rowan stood abruptly, the chair scraping loudly against the floor. The room around him seemed to stretch, the walls bending and warping as if alive. The food on the table rotted before his eyes, mold spreading across the bread, the stew bubbling with dark, viscous liquid. The woman reached for him, her fingers elongating into grotesque talons. He stumbled back, falling against the door, which was no longer solid but pulsating like flesh. A low rumble filled the air, and he turned to see the house collapsing inward, consumed by the encroaching darkness. A voice whispered in his ear: *"You can't escape."* </div> <div class="section nightmare"> Rowan ran, the meadow now replaced by a barren wasteland, the sky above swirling with storm clouds that bled crimson. The river was dry, its bed cracked and filled with bones. The air was filled with ash, each breath searing his lungs. Shadows moved at the edge of his vision, humanoid figures with glowing red eyes and jagged teeth. One stepped forward, its voice a chilling mockery of his own: *"You’re one of us now."* Rowan tried to scream, but no sound came out. The ground beneath him split open, and he fell into a void. The figures followed, their laughter blending into the deafening roar of the abyss. As he fell, images flashed before him: memories of battles fought, faces of those he had failed to save, his own reflection twisted and monstrous. </div> <div class="section dark"> He landed hard on a surface that was neither solid nor stable, a shifting mass of black tendrils that wrapped around his limbs. The air was alive with whispers now, each one accusing him, mocking him: *"You think you’re a hero? You’re nothing."* The tendrils pulled him down, deeper into the darkness. Above him, the sky shattered, revealing an endless void filled with staring eyes. A single voice rose above the chaos, deep and resonant, filled with agony and despair: *"You will never be free. You belong to me."* Rowan struggled, but the more he fought, the tighter the tendrils held him. His vision blurred, the world around him dissolving into nothingness. SOMEBODY PLEASE PULL ME OUT </div> </div> <iframe class="hidden-audio" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/5ygr4AsKEOY?autoplay=1&loop=1&playlist=5ygr4AsKEOY" allow="autoplay" frameborder="0"> </iframe> </body> </html> [[ AWAKEN ]]The faint light of dawn filtered through the cracks in the bunker walls, painting the room in muted hues. Rowan kept shifting, his dreams fading into the recesses of his mind. A soft knock on his bed snapped him fully awake. "It's Redbell," came the voice from the other side, calm but insistent. Rowan sat up, rubbing his eyes before opening the door. Redbell stood there, his expression serious but with a look of reassurance in his sharp green eyes. "Morning," Rowan mumbled. "Morning," Redbell replied, stepping back to let Rowan gather himself. "A man wants to meet you. He's someone who could help you figure out where you stand... with us." "With you?" Rowan asked, still trying to piece things together. "The rebellion," Redbell clarified. "He’s an important figure. Trust me, it’s worth hearing him out. And I’ll explain a few things on the way." Rowan nodded, slipping on his boots and following Redbell down the dimly lit corridor. The air in the bunker felt colder this morning, more charged, as if something significant was about to unfold. As they walked, Redbell spoke quietly, his voice measured. "The rebellion isn’t as unified as we like to pretend," he began. "It’s made up of factions, different groups with different ideals. Some of them want democracy, others want a council. Hell, some think anarchy’s the way to go. But we all share the same goal: to make the Federation a better place." Rowan frowned. "By tearing it apart?" Redbell glanced at him, the corner of his mouth twitching into a faint smile. "Not quite. The Federation’s a machine. A powerful one. But it's rusted, corrupted, and fed by the blood of its own people. We’re not here to destroy it, we’re here to fix it. Some factions have... questionable methods, though. You'll see what I mean soon enough." They entered a larger chamber, one Rowan hadn’t seen before. It was filled with a lot of conversations, the occasional clink of weapons, and the scent of coffee and grease. At the far end of the room, seated at a table, was the scar-faced man Rowan had noticed the day before. His face was a roadmap of battles lost and won, his eyes piercing yet strangely weary. "Rowan, meet Commander Vale," Redbell said, motioning for Rowan to sit across from the man. Commander Vale leaned forward, his hands on the table. "So, you’re the newcomer," he said, his voice gravelly but firm. "I’ve heard a bit about you. Survived a Federation transport. That’s no small feat." Rowan shrugged uncomfortably. "Luck, I guess." Vale’s face twisted into a smirk. "Luck doesn’t get you through what you’ve been through. Let’s not downplay your resilience." He leaned back, studying Rowan for a moment. "We could use someone like you. But first, I need to know... why you’re really here. Is it revenge? Survival? Or something else?" Rowan hesitated, the memories of what the Federation had done to him bubbling to the surface. He clenched his fists under the table. "They took everything from me," he said finally. "Family. Friends. My life. I don’t know if I care about fixing the Federation. But I can’t sit by and do nothing anymore." Vale nodded, his expression unreadable. "Fair answer. Anger can be a good motivator, but it won’t sustain you. If you’re going to fight with us, you’ll need more than that. You’ll need purpose." Redbell, standing by Rowan’s side, interjected. "That’s why I brought him here, Commander." Vale’s eyes shifted to Redbell briefly before returning to Rowan. "Alright. Let’s start with the basics. We don’t force anyone to join. But if you want to make a difference, you’ll have to choose a side. And that choice might not be as simple as you think." Vale stood, gesturing for Rowan to follow. They exited the chamber and entered a long hallway lined with banners, each one bearing the symbol of a different faction. Finally, he stopped in front of a banner with a broken gold crown. "The Broken Crown. They believe the only way to fix the Federation is to tear it down entirely. Start fresh. But chaos has a cost, and not everyone’s willing to pay it." Rowan stood there, staring at the banners, his mind racing. Redbell placed a hand on his shoulder. "Take your time," he said. "Think about what you want. Not just for yourself, but for everyone else who’s counting on us." [[The Broken Crown]]The faint light of dawn filtered through the cracks in the bunker walls, painting the room in muted hues. Rowan hesitated, the memories of what the Federation had done to him bubbling to the surface. He clenched his fists under the table. "They took everything from me," he said finally. "Family. Friends. My life. I don’t know if I care about fixing the Federation. But I can’t sit by and do nothing anymore." Vale nodded, his expression unreadable. "Fair answer. Anger can be a good motivator, but it won’t sustain you. If you’re going to fight with us, you’ll need more than that. You’ll need purpose." Redbell, standing by Rowan’s side, interjected. "That’s why I brought him here, Commander." Vale’s eyes shifted to Redbell briefly before returning to Rowan. "Alright. Let’s start with the basics. We don’t force anyone to join. But if you want to make a difference, you’ll have to choose a side. And that choice might not be as simple as you think." Vale stood, gesturing for Rowan to follow. They exited the chamber and entered a long hallway lined with banners, each one bearing the symbol of a different faction. Finally, he stopped in front of a banner with a broken gold crown. "The Broken Crown. They believe the only way to fix the Federation is to tear it down entirely. Start fresh. But chaos has a cost, and not everyone’s willing to pay it." Rowan stood there, staring at the banners, his mind racing. Redbell placed a hand on his shoulder. "Take your time," he said. "Think about what you want. Not just for yourself, but for everyone else who’s counting on us." [[The Broken Crown ]]The faint light of dawn filtered through the cracks in the bunker walls, painting the room in muted hues. Rowan kept shifting, his dreams fading into the recesses of his mind. A soft knock on his bed snapped him fully awake. "It's Redbell," came the voice from the other side, calm but insistent. Rowan sat up, rubbing his eyes before opening the door. Redbell stood there, his expression serious but with a look of reassurance in his sharp green eyes. "Morning," Rowan mumbled. "Morning," Redbell replied, stepping back to let Rowan gather himself. "A man wants to meet you. He's someone who could help you figure out where you stand... with us." "With you?" Rowan asked, still trying to piece things together. "The rebellion," Redbell clarified. "He’s an important figure. Trust me, it’s worth hearing him out. And I’ll explain a few things on the way." Rowan nodded, slipping on his boots and following Redbell down the dimly lit corridor. The air in the bunker felt colder this morning, more charged, as if something significant was about to unfold. As they walked, Redbell spoke quietly, his voice measured. "The rebellion isn’t as unified as we like to pretend," he began. "It’s made up of factions, different groups with different ideals. Some of them want democracy, others want a council. Hell, some think anarchy’s the way to go. But we all share the same goal: to make the Federation a better place." Rowan frowned. "By tearing it apart?" Redbell glanced at him, the corner of his mouth twitching into a faint smile. "Not quite. The Federation’s a machine. A powerful one. But it's rusted, corrupted, and fed by the blood of its own people. We’re not here to destroy it, we’re here to fix it. Some factions have... questionable methods, though. You'll see what I mean soon enough." They entered a larger chamber, one Rowan hadn’t seen before. It was filled with a lot of conversations, the occasional clink of weapons, and the scent of coffee and grease. At the far end of the room, seated at a table, was the scar-faced man Rowan had noticed the day before. His face was a roadmap of battles lost and won, his eyes piercing yet strangely weary. "Rowan, meet Commander Vale," Redbell said, motioning for Rowan to sit across from the man. Commander Vale leaned forward, his hands on the table. "So, you’re the newcomer," he said, his voice gravelly but firm. "I’ve heard a bit about you. Survived a Federation transport. That’s no small feat." Rowan shrugged uncomfortably. "Luck, I guess." Vale’s face twisted into a smirk. "Luck doesn’t get you through what you’ve been through. Let’s not downplay your resilience." He leaned back, studying Rowan for a moment. "We could use someone like you. But first, I need to know... why you’re really here. Is it revenge? Survival? Or something else?" Rowan hesitated, the memories of what the Federation had done to him bubbling to the surface. He clenched his fists under the table. "They took everything from me," he said finally. "Family. Friends. My life. I don’t know if I care about fixing the Federation. But I can’t sit by and do nothing anymore." Vale nodded, his expression unreadable. "Fair answer. Anger can be a good motivator, but it won’t sustain you. If you’re going to fight with us, you’ll need more than that. You’ll need purpose." Redbell, standing by Rowan’s side, interjected. "That’s why I brought him here, Commander." Vale’s eyes shifted to Redbell briefly before returning to Rowan. "Alright. Let’s start with the basics. We don’t force anyone to join. But if you want to make a difference, you’ll have to choose a side. And that choice might not be as simple as you think." Vale stood, gesturing for Rowan to follow. They exited the chamber and entered a long hallway lined with banners, each one bearing the symbol of a different faction. Finally, he stopped in front of a banner with a broken gold crown. "The Broken Crown. They believe the only way to fix the Federation is to tear it down entirely. Start fresh. But chaos has a cost, and not everyone’s willing to pay it." Rowan stood there, staring at the banners, his mind racing. Redbell placed a hand on his shoulder. "Take your time," he said. "Think about what you want. Not just for yourself, but for everyone else who’s counting on us." [[The Broken Crown ]]The broken, scattered pieces of conversations and the distant voices reverberated off the walls of the crowded hallway. The activity here was unlike any Rowan had encountered before, it felt like a hive of purpose, alive with intention. Vale paused before a heavy door, its surface scratched and worn, the handle worn smooth by countless hands. He turned to Rowan, giving a reassuring nod. “This is it,” he said simply. The door groaned as it slid open, revealing a room that could have once been a grand hall or a meeting space. Now, it was a controlled chaos, with broken furniture and makeshift tables scattered throughout the space. People moved between them, some sitting, others standing. Weapons, tools, and bits of technology littered the space. The room stilled as they entered, eyes lifting from whatever task or conversation they had been involved in. Rowan’s eyes scanned the faces before him. Some were hard, battle-worn, others youthful and full of hunger for something greater. Each person seemed to have a different type of intensity. Vale stepped forward, and as he did, the crowd seemed to part, like a sea shifting to make way for something powerful. The leader of The Broken Crowns stood at the far end of the room, his back to them. He was tall, broad-shouldered, with a hardened face that had seen more than its fair share of battles. His clothing was practical, tactical even, layered with bits of worn armor and accessories that gave him an air of someone who’d seen the world from the outside and came back to claim his place. "Rowan, meet the leader of The Broken Crowns," Vale spoke in a low tone. The leader turned, his eyes sharp, assessing Rowan with a brief but thorough glance. He didn’t smile or offer pleasantries; his demeanor was no-nonsense, as though time was something he had little to spare. Yet there was an undeniable sense of respect. “Welcome to our home, Rowan,” the leader said, his voice deep and calm. “I am known as Talon, the leader of The Broken Crowns. We’re a faction of the overlooked, the discarded, those left behind by the Federation and its chokehold on this world. And you, Rowan, you’ve made a wise choice in seeking us out. Few have the courage to stand against the tide.” Rowan could tell that Talon was sizing him up, just as he had with Vale. There was no judgment in his eyes, as if he were trying to determine whether Rowan was the ally he needed or just another passing face in a crowd. “Thank you,” Rowan said. “I’m here to find a path that aligns with my goals. If you think I’m wise, then we’ll see if we can work together.” Talon gave a slight nod, his face twitching in what could almost have been a smirk. “We don’t offer anyone salvation. You’ll have to carve your own way here. But you’ve chosen right. The Broken Crowns are not just a band of rebels, we’re a force of freedom.” The leader stepped closer, his eyes narrowing as he studied Rowan. “Tell me, Rowan, do you have any experience with weapons? We fight battles where the gun in your hand is as important as the strength in your heart. Not every weapon is a sword or a blade. Some are designed to protect the power structures of the Federation.” Rowan’s expression hardened. “I know my way around a weapon. You can say I’ve been trained.” Talon’s expression softened just a touch, a feeling of approval crossing his features. “Good. Very good. But I hope you’re ready to handle more than just standard issue. These days, a man needs to be prepared for anything, and in our ranks, we need those who can handle more than just the typical.” He motioned to a table near the back of the room, where several high-tech firearms lay scattered. “We have pulse rifles here, Federal ones, designed with biolocks embedded in their algorithms. No one outside the Federation could ever dream of unlocking them. They’re useless unless you’ve been specifically authorized by their DNA protocols. But you’re a wise one, I imagine you’ve thought about that, haven’t you?” Rowan’s brow furrowed. He stepped closer to the table, his fingers grazing the sleek surface of the rifles. They were impressive, no doubt, but it was the lock in their systems that concerned him. “Once again, I know,” he said, eyes fixed on Talon. “But... how could anyone use them if they’re biolocked? You need to be coded, have the Federation’s DNA signatures to even fire them.” Talon chuckled, a low, throaty sound that went around in the quiet room. “Ah, the biolock. The Federation’s most foolproof method of ensuring their weapons only work for their own. They think they’ve cornered the market, don’t they?” He took a step toward Rowan, his eyes glinting with a dangerous knowledge. “We have our ways. The Broken Crowns have no shortage of data jackers, skilled technicians who can rewrite, rework, and unlock just about anything. Federal firearms are no exception. These aren’t just toys, Rowan. They’re tools, weapons designed to hold their own against the might of the Federation. We’ve got some of the best in the business, and they know how to force-unlock those weapons. Trust me when I say... it’s a great weapon to wield.” Rowan nodded slowly, his eyes drifting back to the rifles. It was clear Talon wasn’t just speaking in hypotheticals. This was the reality of their operation. “So, you’ve got people who can hack into the Federation’s system? They can unlock these things and make them usable for anyone?” he asked, intrigued but still cautious. Talon’s lips curled into a smile, though it was more like a snarl. “Not just anyone. But if you’re in our ranks, you’ll be ready to use them. And that’s what counts. You’ll see for yourself soon enough.” Rowan could feel the decision pressing down on him as he looked from Talon to the pulse rifles on the table. This was the kind of weaponry he needed to survive in a world where control was everything, where the Federation held all the cards. And now, with The Broken Crowns, it seemed he might have a chance to tip the scales. “I’m in,” Rowan said, his voice firm. “If you can unlock these weapons, then I’ll fight with you. Let’s see what kind of force we can become.” Talon’s eyes sparkled with approval, and for the first time, his expression softened. “Welcome to The Broken Crowns, Rowan. You’ve chosen well.” Talon leaned back slightly, his hands behind his back as he observed Rowan closely. The room seemed to tighten in anticipation of what was to come. “There’s something I need you to do, Rowan,” he said, the edges of his words heavy with meaning. “A test of sorts. A way for you to prove you’re worthy of our cause.” Rowan straightened, his eyes narrowing slightly as he studied Talon. The leader’s demeanor hadn’t changed; there was no sign of trickery, but there was no mistaking the fact that this task would be crucial. “The factions like to band together to help each other reach their goals, but remember, Rowan, our ideals still differ in the end. One of us will have to take the throne of the Federation if we ever make it to the end of this war. But that’s a distant thought for now. Right now, it’s about proving loyalty to your people, your ideals. You’re going to do something that will set you apart.” Rowan’s jaw clenched slightly. “What’s the job?” Talon continued. “There’s a Broken Crown officer, one of ours, who’s been captured by the Federation. We know where he’s being held, but the detention facility is well-guarded. This isn’t a simple rescue mission, Rowan. You’ll need to be quick, decisive, and ruthless when necessary. We need him back, and I trust you can do it.” Rowan paused, his mind working quickly. He didn’t hesitate for long. “I can do it. I know a guy who’d be perfect for this kind of job.” Talon gave a slight nod of approval, his eyes filled with satisfaction. “Good. You’ll need all the help you can get. I’ll lend you a unit of men who know this mission well. It’s important to me that we gain an edge over the Federation, and this officer is crucial to our cause.” “I agree,” Rowan said, his voice firm and clear. “I’ll get the job done.” Talon nodded again, then gestured to the soldiers in the room. A sergeant stepped forward, his demeanor calm but alert. He was a tall, broad man with a hardened face, eyes that had seen the worst of the world and lived to tell about it. My name’s Mercer, and I know this mission inside and out.” He paused, sizing Rowan up for a moment before continuing. “If you’re up for it, I’ll make sure we get in, get the officer, and get out with minimal hassle.” Rowan gave a small nod. “I appreciate it, Mercer.” As the sergeant made his preparations, Rowan had went out of his way to find the man he wanted to bring, he turned to Kade, the familiar figure he had met in the infirmary. The detention facility’s not far now.” The VTOL descended gradually, avoiding the Federation’s radar systems by skimming low through the clouds. The landing zone was safe for now, but they would need to be careful. As the team disembarked, Mercer led them through the dense underbrush. We’ll get close enough to make a final approach on foot.” Rowan nodded, keeping his eyes sharp. “Who else is in your unit? Who are we working with?” Mercer glanced back, his eyes reflecting the light from the surrounding trees. “We’ve got a recon specialist with us. He’ll be handling any engagements from a distance, sniper support, surveillance, and the like. He’s good, Rowan. You’ll want him on your side.” Rowan raised an eyebrow. “What else?” Mercer kept walking, his pace unbroken. “We’ve got a couple of other specialists, too. A demolitions expert, a tech officer, and a medic. Everyone’s here for a reason. We’ve trained together for this kind of mission. Now we just need to stick to the plan.” The group continued forward, walking through the dense woods with Mercer leading them expertly through the terrain. It was a place where escape was nearly impossible, and survival even harder. The facility itself was complex, a series of high-tech buildings surrounded by electrified fences and heavy security. Watchtowers lined the perimeter, their red lights scanning the area for any signs of movement. Military soldiers patrolled the outer edges, their rifles scanning the terrain actively. Rowan’s eyes caught glimpses of the sentries on the walls, their patrols moving methodically, but they were still far enough away for them to make their move. Mercer’s voice was a whisper in the dark. “We’ll need to approach from the west. There’s a blind spot in their security, and we can use it to slip inside. Once we’re in, we’ll have to move fast. No hesitation.” Rowan nodded, his mind already running through the plan. “Let’s do it.” The team moved through the forest. Mercer, the sergeant, led the way, as he led Rowan and Kade toward the west side of the detention facility. The dense underbrush and towering trees provided some cover, but the path ahead was still fraught with danger. Rowan stayed alert, his mind running through the possible scenarios in his head as they approached their destination. Soon, they reached the designated recon point, a small rise that overlooked the perimeter of the facility. The recon specialist, was already in place, his long-range sniper rifle set up on a tripod and aimed at the facility. "Recon, what's the layout? We need to move in." He barely moved, his eyes scanning the area through his binoculars. "Two guards on each tower, two squads on the ground. Standard patrol routes. The security systems are tight, electrified fences, cameras on every corner. But there’s a gap to the west, a maintenance tunnel beneath the old wall. We can slip through there, but it's going to be a tight squeeze." Rowan studied the area, his mind already mapping out the route. "What about the fence? The alarms on it?" He looked down at his equipment, tapping his screen. "The fence has a control box nearby, looks like a manual override for the alarms. We’ll need to disable it before crossing." As they moved deeper into the tunnel, the walls seemed to close in, the tightness of the space adding to the sense of urgency. Soon, they reached a set of rusted doors that led into the prison complex. Kade reached for the control panel beside the door, his fingers moving with ease as he attempted to hack into the system. A low buzz sounded, then a click. The door slid open, revealing a dimly lit corridor on the other side. The walls were lined with reinforced doors, the prison’s inner sanctum. It’s going to be tight, but we have a good shot if we move quickly.” As they moved deeper into the prison. But for now, they remained undetected, slipping through the shadows as Mercer led them deeper into the facility. But as they neared their destination, a sudden problem arose. His eyes scanned the surroundings quickly. "We need a way out, now. If we don’t move fast enough, we’ll get spotted. But we can’t let that happen." Rowan led the way, looking out for potential obstacles while Kade monitored their position on a compact schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. After navigating through several turns and drops, they found an opening that overlooked a dimly lit staff room. Below, a massive industrial fan dominated one wall, its blades spinning lazily as it cycled cool air throughout the facility. Rowan signaled for a stop and gestured for Kade to move forward. The engineer crawled beside him and peered through the grate. "That fan leads to the room where the officer is being held," Kade whispered. "It’s our way in." As Kade worked on loosening the grate, Mercer and Tessa took up defensive positions, watching the narrow vent for any sign of pursuit. Just as Kade finished removing the final bolt, Mercer froze. He raised a fist, a universal signal to halt. Everyone immediately went still. From below, the sound of heavy boots went through the room. The squad peered through the slats of the grate as the door swung open, revealing three massive figures. (text-colour:red)[Elite Honor Guards. ] The guards strode into the room. Their crimson cloaks swayed as they walked, the polished surface of their monotech goggles reflecting the dim light. Each one stood nearly eight feet tall. The leader of the trio carried an unsettling weapon at his side, a hilt that pulsed faintly with crimson light. Rowan tensed as the guards approached the Broken Crown Officer, who sat shackled to a heavy chair in the center of the room. Despite his injuries, the officer held his head high, his defiance undimmed. The lead Honor Guard’s voice was a low, mechanical growl as he spoke. "We’ll ask one more time: What are your group’s intentions against High Command?" The officer sneered, blood dripping from a cut on his lip. "Go to hell." One of the guards stepped forward, the weapon at his side activating with a menacing snap-hiss. A crimson, unstable blade burst to life, its jagged edges crackling with raw energy. The guard brought it dangerously close to the officer’s face, the heat of the blade causing beads of sweat to form on the officer’s forehead. "Talk," the guard demanded, his voice laced with menace. "What do you know about the Federation’s defenses? What’s your plan?" Rowan glanced at Mercer, who had already drawn his silenced weapon. A single nod from Rowan was all the confirmation Mercer needed. Kade leaned close to Rowan and whispered, "The fan’s ready, but we’ve got to move fast." "Stay here and hold the vent for us," Rowan ordered. "We’ll need you to deploy the ladder when it’s time to exfil." Rowan signaled to the squad, and one by one, they silently descended into the staff room, using the now-stationary fan as their entry point. The first guard barely had time to register the faint shuffle of footsteps before Rowan’s blade pierced through the gap between his helmet and chest armor. The massive figure collapsed with a heavy thud. The second guard turned, raising his weapon, but Mercer’s silenced shot struck him squarely in the visor, shattering the monotech goggles and dropping him instantly. The third guard roared in rage, igniting his lightsaber as he lunged at Rowan. The unstable blade hissed and crackled, narrowly missing its mark. Rowan ducked beneath the swing and retaliated with a precise upward slash, his blade finding the vulnerable joint beneath the guard’s arm. The giant staggered, and Mercer delivered the final blow, her combat knife driving into the base of his skull. The room fell silent save for the faint hum of the deactivated lightsaber. Mercer nudged one of the fallen guards with his boot, his brow furrowed. "That was too easy," he muttered. "Elite Honor Guards are supposed to put up more of a fight." Before Rowan could respond, the shrill wail of an alarm pierced the air, bathing the room in a pulsating red light. "Time’s up!" Kade shouted from above. "We’ve got company, move!" The squad acted quickly, freeing the Broken Crown Officer from his restraints. The man was weak, but he managed to stand with their support. "Up the ladder, now!" Rowan barked, shoving the officer toward the deployable ladder Kade had lowered into the room. He quickly reattached the fan, its blades whirring back to life just as the sound of boots thundered into the staff room below. From their hidden vantage point, Rowan watched as a squad of federal soldiers stormed into the room, their weapons drawn. They froze at the sight of the three dead Honor Guards. "Targets are gone," one of the soldiers reported, his voice tense. "The Honor Guards... they’re down. Repeat, they’re tagged as dead!" The squad went on, the distant alarms fading behind them as they disappeared into the vents, their mission far from over. With the Broken Crown Officer secured and the fan blades spinning once again, the squad moved swiftly back into the ventilation system. Drowned out by the blaring alarms going through the base. Red emergency lights pulsing in synchrony, casting shadows through the vents and grates. “Kade, how far?” Rowan whispered sharply. “Two more turns, then straight to the exit,” Kade replied, his eyes glued to the schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. Sweat dripped from his brow as he crawled ahead. Mercer helped the officer along, the man limping but still determined to escape. The officer’s breathing was labored, his face pale, but he said nothing, pushing himself to keep up. Mercer activated his comm softly. “Recon, status?” “Perimeter’s swarming,” Recon replied in his usual calm tone. “Looks like they’re doing a sweep of the forest edge. I’ve taken out a few already. No chatter yet, seems they haven’t realized their comms are dead.” “Keep it that way,” Rowan interjected, his tone firm. “We can’t afford them calling for reinforcements here.” From his elevated vantage point outside the compound, Recon adjusted his scope. The digital display of his rifle overlaid critical information as he scanned the area. A group of guards patrolling near the main gate came into view. One guard paused, looking in the direction of the forest. Recon exhaled slowly, steadying his aim. The suppressor muffled the crack of his rifle as the first guard dropped silently, a clean shot through the neck. The second guard turned, his expression frozen in surprise, just as another shot found its hit. “Two down.” Recon murmured. “Keep moving. I’ll handle anyone who gets too close.” Inside the vent, the squad reached the final stretch leading to their entry point. The faint glow of moonlight spilled through the grate. “Kade, get that panel open,” Mercer ordered. Kade moved quickly, pulling out a compact tool to unscrew the bolts holding the grate in place. With a soft creak, it came loose, and he set it aside carefully. “Let’s go,” Rowan said, gesturing for Mercer and the officer to move first. The squad emerged into the open air, crouching low as they used the surrounding shadows for cover. The forest was ahead. “Recon, eyes up,” Rowan said. “Already on it,” Recon replied. He scanned the area again, spotting a pair of guards near a communications dish. One of them reached for his radio, likely to report in they found the team running away. ''Not happening. '' Recon adjusted his scope and fired, the first shot dropping the guard instantly. The second guard froze, looking around frantically before falling moments later. “Clear,” Recon confirmed. “You’re good to move. Stay low.” Mercer led the group into the forest, the dense canopy swallowing them in darkness. The officer stumbled once, but Mercer caught him, supporting him with an arm around his shoulders. The alarms from the base faded as they ventured deeper into the woods. The only sounds now were the rustling of leaves underfoot and the occasional distant call of wildlife. After what felt like hours, they reached the extraction point. The VTOL was already waiting, its engines sounding softly as its faint lights illuminated the clearing. “Move, move,” Mercer urged, helping the officer climb aboard. Rowan and Kade kept watch, their weapons focused on the treeline until everyone was safely inside. With a sharp hiss, the VTOL’s doors slid shut, and the craft lifted off, its engines roaring to life as it ascended into the night sky. Rowan exhaled deeply, leaning against the bulkhead as the adrenaline began to wear off. The officer, seated across from him, looked up with tired but grateful eyes. “Thank you,” the officer said, his voice heavy with emotion. “If you hadn’t come, I wouldn’t have lasted another day in there. I’ve been gathering intel for weeks... This is going to change everything.” Rowan managed a faint smile, nodding. “Glad we could help.” The VTOL soared over the forest, the lights of the enemy base growing faint in the distance. Inside, the squad allowed themselves a moment to decompress. Mercer checked his weapon, Tessa leaned back with her eyes closed, and Kade wiped sweat from his brow, glancing at the officer with a nod of respect. They landed at the Broken Crown outpost just as the sun dipped below the horizon. The VTOL’s doors hissed open, and the squad emerged. The officer, sided by Mercer and Kade, walked with a very relieved stride. Talon awaited them at the entrance of the bunker. “You made it back. Well done. I am impressed you are all still alive.” The officer stepped forward. He reached into his pocket and retrieved a small, black data chip, holding it out toward Talon. “This is everything I’ve gathered over the past month. Movement patterns, supply chains, and, most critically, details on a transport coming from the Citadel. Whatever they’re moving is big, and they’ve gone to extreme lengths to protect it. They have a lot of Elite Honor Guards escorting it.” Talon took the chip, inspecting it briefly before sliding it into a reader attached to his wrist device. His eyes narrowed as he skimmed the initial files, the faint glow of the screen illuminating his hardened features. After a moment, Talon looked up. “If this transport is as important as you claim, why didn’t they wipe your memory after the intel was secured?” The officer hesitated, his hand brushing instinctively against his temple. “They couldn’t risk it. I made sure the data was encrypted in a way that required my own neural patterns to decode. It was risky, but it worked. They need me intact to access what I know.” Kade, standing off to the side, let out a low whistle. “Smart move. But now you’re a walking target.” The officer nodded. “Exactly. If this transport reaches its destination, it could shift the balance of this entire quiet war. We have to intercept it. The Citadel doesn't usually transport anything out from it.” Talon’s brow furrowed as he processed the information. “What are they transporting?” The officer shook his head. “I don’t know for certain. What I do know is that it’s classified at the highest level. I’ve heard whispers in the prison, something about a prototype weapon, or maybe even a key Federation official being relocated. Either way, it’s vital enough for them to send one of their armored convoys straight from the Citadel.” Rowan, who had been silently observing, stepped forward. “If we intercept this convoy, it could give us leverage. Even if it’s not a weapon, capturing someone high up could tip the scales in our favor.” Talon nodded slowly. “Agreed. But this won’t be a simple hit-and-run. Federation convoys are fortified, and their escorts are ruthless. We’ll need a plan that doesn’t rely on brute force.” Mercer crossed his arms, his tone skeptical. “And what’s the timetable on this transport? We can’t just stumble into this unprepared.” The officer checked his wrist device, bringing up a holographic map of the surrounding area. A blinking red dot marked the convoy’s projected route. “It’s scheduled to pass through Sector 12 in Ontario in twelve hours. That gives us enough time to plan an ambush if we move quickly.” Talon’s lips curved into a faint, almost predatory smile. “Good. We’ll gather the team and prepare. This might be the opening we’ve been waiting for.” He turned to Rowan, his expression softening slightly. “You’ve earned your place here. And now, you’ll get the chance to prove it again. We will take the Transporter.” Rowan’s eyes widened. “Understood, sir.” Talon clapped him on the shoulder. “We’ll need every ounce of skill you’ve got, soldier. Dismissed.” Rowan nodded and made his way to the dormitory. As he reached his bunk, he sat down heavily, his mind racing with thoughts of the mission ahead. He knew there was no room for hesitation. The moment the call came, the bunker was a whirlwind of motion. Activity filled the hallways as everyone scrambled to prepare for probably the most critical mission the rebellion had faced. There was no turning back now. Rowan grabbed his gear, his heart pounding in his chest. Today, they would make their move against the Federation. Today, they would strike at the Citadel’s artery. Rowan had heard whispers of the hangar bay deep beneath the surface, but nothing had prepared him for the vast scale of it. When he and Kade arrived, the sheer size of the underground facility took his breath away. The bunker’s architecture was nothing short of breathtaking. What appeared to be a cavernous space had been transformed into a state-of-the-art military hub, high-tech, secure, and almost impossibly vast for being so deep beneath the earth’s surface. The ceiling stretched far above them, crisscrossed with thick beams of reinforced metal, while the floor was a maze of launch pads, storage areas, and repair bays. Every inch of the hangar was carefully designed, the space clearly having been constructed over years of painstaking work. It was hard for Rowan to wrap his mind around the fact that this was an underground facility, let alone the fact that a place this grand was hidden beneath miles of earth and rock. The rebels had truly built something remarkable here, something that would give them a fighting chance. The sleek, black craft, its sharp edges and advanced design making it look more like a predator ready to strike than a simple transport vehicle. The Manticore belonged to the Federation. The Manticore was quick, stealthy, and ideally suited for the mission. Its low profile would make it difficult for anyone to track once they were airborne, and it was equipped with all the necessary tools to make the trip to Sector 13 undetected. But there was one problem: they weren’t the Federation. They were a ragtag group of rebels, and every move they made had to be measured. The team filed in behind him, taking their seats as the engines hummed to life, a low growl that vibrated through the hull. A quick briefing followed: they were to pose as a cargo drop-off ship from the Federation, nothing more. Their target was Sector 13, and they needed to blend in with the regular transport convoys until they could intercept the Citadel transport. It had to be quick, clean, and, most importantly, undetected. The roof of the hangar slowly began to slide open as the Manticore lifted off. The sky above them revealed itself, a dark, clouded expanse that stretched on infinitely. Wind rushed through the open hatch as the craft rose, the rumble of its engines vibrating through the air. They were on their way. "Stay sharp," Kade’s voice came over the comms, low but steady. "We’re about to hit Federation airspace." If they made even the slightest mistake, the entire mission would be compromised. The Federation wouldn’t be fooled for long. They were going to have to pull off this ruse with a level of skill and deceit that would make even the most seasoned operatives impressed. Before the inspector could react, the rebel swiftly knocked him out, the sudden movement so quick and precise it was as if they’d rehearsed it a hundred times. Rowan didn’t flinch. They couldn’t afford hesitation. They had to be swift, lethal, and efficient. The team moved like a well-oiled machine, flowing out of the Manticore and into the darkness, disappearing into the shadows of the landing zone. The Citadel transport had just arrived, guarded by two heavily armored Elite Honor Guard vehicles, their presence a clear sign of how important this shipment was. The gunman in the front was alert, scanning for threats, while another sat in the back, watching the horizon. Rowan’s heart raced. The Elite Honor Guards were dangerous. Any misstep could spell disaster. The team huddled in a nearby alcove, blending into the surroundings as they waited for the transport to pass. The Honor Guards were too skilled—they could spot even the smallest anomaly in the shadows. One wrong move, and their mission would end before it had even begun. We’re a faction of the overlooked, the discarded, those left behind by the Federation and its chokehold on this world. And you, Rowan, you’ve made a wise choice in seeking us out. Few have the courage to stand against the tide.” Rowan could tell that Talon was sizing him up, just as he had with Vale. The Federation’s most foolproof method of ensuring their weapons only work for their own. They’re tools, weapons designed to hold their own against the might of the Federation. We’ve got some of the best in the business, and they know how to force-unlock those weapons. They can unlock these things and make them usable for anyone?” he asked, intrigued but still cautious. Talon’s lips curled into a smile, though it was more like a snarl. “Not just anyone. But if you’re in our ranks, you’ll be ready to use them. And that’s what counts. You’ll see for yourself soon enough.” Rowan could feel the decision pressing down on him as he looked from Talon to the pulse rifles on the table. This was the kind of weaponry he needed to survive in a world where control was everything, where the Federation held all the cards. And now, with The Broken Crowns, it seemed he might have a chance to tip the scales. “I’m in,” Rowan said, his voice firm. “If you can unlock these weapons, then I’ll fight with you. Let’s see what kind of force we can become.” Talon’s eyes sparkled with approval, and for the first time, his expression softened. “Welcome to The Broken Crowns, Rowan. You’ve chosen well.” Talon leaned back slightly, his hands behind his back as he observed Rowan closely. The room seemed to tighten in anticipation of what was to come. “There’s something I need you to do, Rowan,” he said, the edges of his words heavy with meaning. “A test of sorts. A way for you to prove you’re worthy of our cause.” Rowan straightened, his eyes narrowing slightly as he studied Talon. The leader’s demeanor hadn’t changed; there was no sign of trickery, but there was no mistaking the fact that this task would be crucial. “The factions like to band together to help each other reach their goals, but remember, Rowan, our ideals still differ in the end. One of us will have to take the throne of the Federation if we ever make it to the end of this war. But that’s a distant thought for now. Right now, it’s about proving loyalty to your people, your ideals. You’re going to do something that will set you apart.” Rowan’s jaw clenched slightly. “What’s the job?” Talon continued. “There’s a Broken Crown officer, one of ours, who’s been captured by the Federation. We know where he’s being held, but the detention facility is well-guarded. This isn’t a simple rescue mission, Rowan. You’ll need to be quick, decisive, and ruthless when necessary. We need him back, and I trust you can do it.” Rowan paused, his mind working quickly. He didn’t hesitate for long. “I can do it. I know a guy who’d be perfect for this kind of job.” Talon gave a slight nod of approval, his eyes filled with satisfaction. “Good. You’ll need all the help you can get. I’ll lend you a unit of men who know this mission well. It’s important to me that we gain an edge over the Federation, and this officer is crucial to our cause.” “I agree,” Rowan said, his voice firm and clear. “I’ll get the job done.” Talon nodded again, then gestured to the soldiers in the room. A sergeant stepped forward, his demeanor calm but alert. He was a tall, broad man with a hardened face, eyes that had seen the worst of the world and lived to tell about it. The sergeant spoke first, his voice a low rumble. “I’ll be delighted to show you the way, Rowan. My name’s Mercer, and I know this mission inside and out.” He paused, sizing Rowan up for a moment before continuing. “If you’re up for it, I’ll make sure we get in, get the officer, and get out with minimal hassle.” Rowan gave a small nod. “I appreciate it, Mercer.” As the sergeant made his preparations, Rowan had went out of his way to find the man he wanted to bring, he turned to Kade, the familiar figure he had met in the infirmary. Kade was sitting near the back, checking over his gear. When Rowan’s eyes found him, Kade’s head snapped up. Recognition was in his eyes, followed by a knowing smile. “Hey, Kade,” Rowan called, his voice steady. “You want to join us on a search-and-rescue mission?” Kade grinned, standing up to join Rowan. “Hell yeah, I’m in. The Broken Crowns could use an engineer. I’m your man.” Rowan could already sense that Kade’s skills would be invaluable. As a former Federal engineer, Kade was uniquely qualified to help them navigate the more technical aspects of their mission. Together, they would form a strong team, one that could handle both combat and the intricacies of the Federation’s security systems. With everything set, the team made their way out to the VTOL waiting outside. The sky was dark, with clouds drifting lazily across the horizon. The VTOL’s engines was soft in the night air as the team boarded. The sleek, black vehicle was built for stealth, designed to blend in with the darkness and avoid detection. Its engines whined as it took off, lifting the group into the night sky and heading toward their destination. The trip was mostly silent, save for the occasional exchange of words between the team. Mercer was focused on the mission. Rowan and Kade sat together, going over the details of the mission. Rowan explained the situation to Kade, who nodded along, already brainstorming ways to get past the Federation’s security systems. “The Federation won’t make this easy,” Kade said, adjusting his gear. “But I’ll be able to work with whatever you throw at me. I’ve dealt with worse.” Mercer’s voice broke through their conversation. “We’re getting close. The detention facility’s not far now.” The VTOL descended gradually, avoiding the Federation’s radar systems by skimming low through the clouds. It touched down in a secluded area, between several mountains, its engines powering down as they landed in a small, hidden clearing. The landing zone was safe for now, but they would need to be careful. As the team disembarked, Mercer led them through the dense underbrush. Rowan took in the surroundings as they moved, the dense forest around them adding to the sense of isolation. After a few minutes, Mercer spoke again, his voice low. “Not far now. We’ll get close enough to make a final approach on foot.” Rowan nodded, keeping his eyes sharp. “Who else is in your unit? Who are we working with?” Mercer glanced back, his eyes reflecting the light from the surrounding trees. “We’ve got a recon specialist with us. He’ll be handling any engagements from a distance, sniper support, surveillance, and the like. He’s good, Rowan. You’ll want him on your side.” Rowan raised an eyebrow. “What else?” Mercer kept walking, his pace unbroken. “We’ve got a couple of other specialists, too. A demolitions expert, a tech officer, and a medic. Everyone’s here for a reason. We’ve trained together for this kind of mission. Now we just need to stick to the plan.” The group continued forward, walking through the dense woods with Mercer leading them expertly through the terrain. Rowan glanced over at Kade. “We’ll be good,” Rowan said. “Kade’s a Federal engineer. He’ll be able to hack into their systems if need be.” Kade gave a small grin. “That’s the plan. But I’m not the only one with tricks up my sleeve.” As the group made their way closer to the facility. they could see the lights of the detention facility in the distance. It was a massive structure, built to contain high-value prisoners, a fortress surrounded by high walls and guarded by Federation soldiers. The sight of it sent a shiver down Rowan’s spine. It was a place where escape was nearly impossible, and survival even harder. The facility itself was complex, a series of high-tech buildings surrounded by electrified fences and heavy security. Watchtowers lined the perimeter, their red lights scanning the area for any signs of movement. Military soldiers patrolled the outer edges, their rifles scanning the terrain actively. Rowan’s eyes caught glimpses of the sentries on the walls, their patrols moving methodically, but they were still far enough away for them to make their move. Mercer’s voice was a whisper in the dark. “We’ll need to approach from the west. There’s a blind spot in their security, and we can use it to slip inside. Once we’re in, we’ll have to move fast. No hesitation.” Rowan nodded, his mind already running through the plan. “Let’s do it.” The team moved through the forest. Mercer, the sergeant, led the way, as he led Rowan and Kade toward the west side of the detention facility. The dense underbrush and towering trees provided some cover, but the path ahead was still fraught with danger. Rowan stayed alert, his mind running through the possible scenarios in his head as they approached their destination. Soon, they reached the designated recon point, a small rise that overlooked the perimeter of the facility. The recon specialist, was already in place, his long-range sniper rifle set up on a tripod and aimed at the facility. His eyes were locked on the movement of the guards below, monitoring their patrol routes. His presence was ghostlike, blending seamlessly into the night. Mercer spoke low, his voice steady. "Recon, what's the layout? We need to move in." He barely moved, his eyes scanning the area through his binoculars. "Two guards on each tower, two squads on the ground. Standard patrol routes. The security systems are tight, electrified fences, cameras on every corner. But there’s a gap to the west, a maintenance tunnel beneath the old wall. We can slip through there, but it's going to be a tight squeeze." Rowan studied the area, his mind already mapping out the route. "What about the fence? The alarms on it?" He looked down at his equipment, tapping his screen. "The fence has a control box nearby, looks like a manual override for the alarms. We’ll need to disable it before crossing." Kade spoke up, his voice calm but with a hint of excitement. "I can handle that. I’ve worked with this tech before. Shouldn’t be a problem." Mercer nodded, stepping aside. "Good. Take the lead, Kade. We’re counting on you." Kade gave a small grin and moved forward, checking his tools and his gear as they advanced. Rowan stayed close, his eyes darting between Kade and the patrolling guards. They had to stay low, and the slightest misstep could mean disaster. As they approached the maintenance tunnel, Kade was already at work. He crouched down beside a set of exposed wires near the fence, his hands moving swiftly over the control panel. His eyes flicked back to Rowan. "This is it. I’m shutting off the fence alarms. But listen," he added in a hushed tone, "the Federation soldiers are all equipped with bio-sensors. If one of them flatlines, the alarms will go off, and they’ll be on us in seconds." Rowan nodded. "Understood." The seconds stretched out as Kade worked quickly, his hands flying over the control panel. A soft click went through the silence as the alarms on the fence went quiet, signaling that they could move. Mercer whispered, "Move." They slipped through the hole Kade had created, crawling beneath the electrified fence and into the cramped maintenance tunnel. The air was musty, stale from years of disuse, but it provided the cover they needed. They moved quickly, following Mercer’s lead as he navigated the dark, narrow passage. As they moved deeper into the tunnel, the walls seemed to close in, the tightness of the space adding to the sense of urgency. Soon, they reached a set of rusted doors that led into the prison complex. Kade reached for the control panel beside the door, his fingers moving with ease as he attempted to hack into the system. A low buzz sounded, then a click. The door slid open, revealing a dimly lit corridor on the other side. The walls were lined with reinforced doors, the prison’s inner sanctum. Mercer signaled for them to move forward. “We’ve got to move fast. The officer is being held in the lower levels. It’s going to be tight, but we have a good shot if we move quickly.” As they moved deeper into the prison. The faint sounds of guards patrolling could be heard down the hall, and every corner they passed could hide an enemy. But for now, they remained undetected, slipping through the shadows as Mercer led them deeper into the facility. But as they neared their destination, a sudden problem arose. A pair of guards appeared in the hallway ahead. The group froze, their bodies tensing as they tried to find a way to remain undetected. Mercer held up his hand, signaling them to stop. His eyes scanned the surroundings quickly. "We need a way out, now. If we don’t move fast enough, we’ll get spotted. But we can’t let that happen." [[ Straight Ahead ]] [[ Ventilation Shaft ]]The broken, scattered pieces of conversations and the distant voices reverberated off the walls of the crowded hallway. The activity here was unlike any Rowan had encountered before, it felt like a hive of purpose, alive with intention. Vale paused before a heavy door, its surface scratched and worn, the handle worn smooth by countless hands. He turned to Rowan, giving a reassuring nod. “This is it,” he said simply. The door groaned as it slid open, revealing a room that could have once been a grand hall or a meeting space. Now, it was a controlled chaos, with broken furniture and makeshift tables scattered throughout the space. People moved between them, some sitting, others standing. Weapons, tools, and bits of technology littered the space. The room stilled as they entered, eyes lifting from whatever task or conversation they had been involved in. Rowan’s eyes scanned the faces before him. Some were hard, battle-worn, others youthful and full of hunger for something greater. Each person seemed to have a different type of intensity. Vale stepped forward, and as he did, the crowd seemed to part, like a sea shifting to make way for something powerful. The leader of The Broken Crowns stood at the far end of the room, his back to them. He was tall, broad-shouldered, with a hardened face that had seen more than its fair share of battles. His clothing was practical, tactical even, layered with bits of worn armor and accessories that gave him an air of someone who’d seen the world from the outside and came back to claim his place. "Rowan, meet the leader of The Broken Crowns," Vale spoke in a low tone. The leader turned, his eyes sharp, assessing Rowan with a brief but thorough glance. He didn’t smile or offer pleasantries; his demeanor was no-nonsense, as though time was something he had little to spare. Yet there was an undeniable sense of respect. “Welcome to our home, Rowan,” the leader said, his voice deep and calm. “I am known as Talon, the leader of The Broken Crowns. We’re a faction of the overlooked, the discarded, those left behind by the Federation and its chokehold on this world. And you, Rowan, you’ve made a wise choice in seeking us out. Few have the courage to stand against the tide.” Rowan could tell that Talon was sizing him up, just as he had with Vale. There was no judgment in his eyes, as if he were trying to determine whether Rowan was the ally he needed or just another passing face in a crowd. “Thank you,” Rowan said. “I’m here to find a path that aligns with my goals. If you think I’m wise, then we’ll see if we can work together.” Talon gave a slight nod, his face twitching in what could almost have been a smirk. “We don’t offer anyone salvation. You’ll have to carve your own way here. But you’ve chosen right. The Broken Crowns are not just a band of rebels, we’re a force of freedom.” The leader stepped closer, his eyes narrowing as he studied Rowan. “Tell me, Rowan, do you have any experience with weapons? We fight battles where the gun in your hand is as important as the strength in your heart. Not every weapon is a sword or a blade. Some are designed to protect the power structures of the Federation.” Rowan’s expression hardened. “I know my way around a weapon. You can say I’ve been trained.” Talon’s expression softened just a touch, a feeling of approval crossing his features. “Good. Very good. But I hope you’re ready to handle more than just standard issue. These days, a man needs to be prepared for anything, and in our ranks, we need those who can handle more than just the typical.” He motioned to a table near the back of the room, where several high-tech firearms lay scattered. “We have pulse rifles here, Federal ones, designed with biolocks embedded in their algorithms. No one outside the Federation could ever dream of unlocking them. They’re useless unless you’ve been specifically authorized by their DNA protocols. But you’re a wise one, I imagine you’ve thought about that, haven’t you?” Rowan’s brow furrowed. He stepped closer to the table, his fingers grazing the sleek surface of the rifles. They were impressive, no doubt, but it was the lock in their systems that concerned him. “Once again, I know,” he said, eyes fixed on Talon. “But... how could anyone use them if they’re biolocked? You need to be coded, have the Federation’s DNA signatures to even fire them.” Talon chuckled, a low, throaty sound that went around in the quiet room. “Ah, the biolock. The Federation’s most foolproof method of ensuring their weapons only work for their own. They think they’ve cornered the market, don’t they?” He took a step toward Rowan, his eyes glinting with a dangerous knowledge. “We have our ways. The Broken Crowns have no shortage of data jackers, skilled technicians who can rewrite, rework, and unlock just about anything. Federal firearms are no exception. These aren’t just toys, Rowan. They’re tools, weapons designed to hold their own against the might of the Federation. We’ve got some of the best in the business, and they know how to force-unlock those weapons. Trust me when I say... it’s a great weapon to wield.” Rowan nodded slowly, his eyes drifting back to the rifles. It was clear Talon wasn’t just speaking in hypotheticals. This was the reality of their operation. “So, you’ve got people who can hack into the Federation’s system? They can unlock these things and make them usable for anyone?” he asked, intrigued but still cautious. Talon’s lips curled into a smile, though it was more like a snarl. “Not just anyone. But if you’re in our ranks, you’ll be ready to use them. And that’s what counts. You’ll see for yourself soon enough.” Rowan could feel the decision pressing down on him as he looked from Talon to the pulse rifles on the table. This was the kind of weaponry he needed to survive in a world where control was everything, where the Federation held all the cards. And now, with The Broken Crowns, it seemed he might have a chance to tip the scales. “I’m in,” Rowan said, his voice firm. “If you can unlock these weapons, then I’ll fight with you. Let’s see what kind of force we can become.” Talon’s eyes sparkled with approval, and for the first time, his expression softened. “Welcome to The Broken Crowns, Rowan. You’ve chosen well.” Talon leaned back slightly, his hands behind his back as he observed Rowan closely. The room seemed to tighten in anticipation of what was to come. “There’s something I need you to do, Rowan,” he said, the edges of his words heavy with meaning. “A test of sorts. A way for you to prove you’re worthy of our cause.” Rowan straightened, his eyes narrowing slightly as he studied Talon. The leader’s demeanor hadn’t changed; there was no sign of trickery, but there was no mistaking the fact that this task would be crucial. “The factions like to band together to help each other reach their goals, but remember, Rowan, our ideals still differ in the end. One of us will have to take the throne of the Federation if we ever make it to the end of this war. But that’s a distant thought for now. Right now, it’s about proving loyalty to your people, your ideals. You’re going to do something that will set you apart.” Rowan’s jaw clenched slightly. “What’s the job?” Talon continued. “There’s a Broken Crown officer, one of ours, who’s been captured by the Federation. We know where he’s being held, but the detention facility is well-guarded. This isn’t a simple rescue mission, Rowan. You’ll need to be quick, decisive, and ruthless when necessary. We need him back, and I trust you can do it.” Rowan paused, his mind working quickly. He didn’t hesitate for long. “I can do it. I know a guy who’d be perfect for this kind of job.” Talon gave a slight nod of approval, his eyes filled with satisfaction. “Good. You’ll need all the help you can get. I’ll lend you a unit of men who know this mission well.
