Trust me when I say... it’s a great weapon to wield.” Rowan nodded slowly, his eyes drifting back to the rifles. It was clear Talon wasn’t just speaking in hypotheticals. This was the reality of their operation. “So, you’ve got people who can hack into the Federation’s system? They can unlock these things and make them usable for anyone?” he asked, intrigued but still cautious. Talon’s lips curled into a smile, though it was more like a snarl. “Not just anyone. But if you’re in our ranks, you’ll be ready to use them. And that’s what counts. You’ll see for yourself soon enough.” Rowan could feel the decision pressing down on him as he looked from Talon to the pulse rifles on the table. This was the kind of weaponry he needed to survive in a world where control was everything, where the Federation held all the cards. And now, with The Broken Crowns, it seemed he might have a chance to tip the scales. “I’m in,” Rowan said, his voice firm. “If you can unlock these weapons, then I’ll fight with you. Let’s see what kind of force we can become.” Talon’s eyes sparkled with approval, and for the first time, his expression softened. “Welcome to The Broken Crowns, Rowan. You’ve chosen well.” Talon leaned back slightly, his hands behind his back as he observed Rowan closely. The room seemed to tighten in anticipation of what was to come. “There’s something I need you to do, Rowan,” he said, the edges of his words heavy with meaning. “A test of sorts. A way for you to prove you’re worthy of our cause.” Rowan straightened, his eyes narrowing slightly as he studied Talon. The leader’s demeanor hadn’t changed; there was no sign of trickery, but there was no mistaking the fact that this task would be crucial. “The factions like to band together to help each other reach their goals, but remember, Rowan, our ideals still differ in the end. One of us will have to take the throne of the Federation if we ever make it to the end of this war. But that’s a distant thought for now. Right now, it’s about proving loyalty to your people, your ideals. You’re going to do something that will set you apart.” Rowan’s jaw clenched slightly. “What’s the job?” Talon continued. “There’s a Broken Crown officer, one of ours, who’s been captured by the Federation. We know where he’s being held, but the detention facility is well-guarded. This isn’t a simple rescue mission, Rowan. You’ll need to be quick, decisive, and ruthless when necessary. We need him back, and I trust you can do it.” Rowan paused, his mind working quickly. He didn’t hesitate for long. “I can do it. I know a guy who’d be perfect for this kind of job.” Talon gave a slight nod of approval, his eyes filled with satisfaction. “Good. You’ll need all the help you can get. I’ll lend you a unit of men who know this mission well. It’s important to me that we gain an edge over the Federation, and this officer is crucial to our cause.” “I agree,” Rowan said, his voice firm and clear. “I’ll get the job done.” Talon nodded again, then gestured to the soldiers in the room. A sergeant stepped forward, his demeanor calm but alert. He was a tall, broad man with a hardened face, eyes that had seen the worst of the world and lived to tell about it. The sergeant spoke first, his voice a low rumble. “I’ll be delighted to show you the way, Rowan. My name’s Mercer, and I know this mission inside and out.” He paused, sizing Rowan up for a moment before continuing. “If you’re up for it, I’ll make sure we get in, get the officer, and get out with minimal hassle.” Rowan gave a small nod. “I appreciate it, Mercer.” As the sergeant made his preparations, Rowan had went out of his way to find the man he wanted to bring, he turned to Kade, the familiar figure he had met in the infirmary. Kade was sitting near the back, checking over his gear. When Rowan’s eyes found him, Kade’s head snapped up. Recognition was in his eyes, followed by a knowing smile. “Hey, Kade,” Rowan called, his voice steady. “You want to join us on a search-and-rescue mission?” Kade grinned, standing up to join Rowan. “Hell yeah, I’m in. The Broken Crowns could use an engineer. I’m your man.” Rowan could already sense that Kade’s skills would be invaluable. As a former Federal engineer, Kade was uniquely qualified to help them navigate the more technical aspects of their mission. Together, they would form a strong team, one that could handle both combat and the intricacies of the Federation’s security systems. With everything set, the team made their way out to the VTOL waiting outside. The sky was dark, with clouds drifting lazily across the horizon. The VTOL’s engines was soft in the night air as the team boarded. The sleek, black vehicle was built for stealth, designed to blend in with the darkness and avoid detection. Its engines whined as it took off, lifting the group into the night sky and heading toward their destination. The trip was mostly silent, save for the occasional exchange of words between the team. Mercer was focused on the mission. Rowan and Kade sat together, going over the details of the mission. Rowan explained the situation to Kade, who nodded along, already brainstorming ways to get past the Federation’s security systems. “The Federation won’t make this easy,” Kade said, adjusting his gear. “But I’ll be able to work with whatever you throw at me. I’ve dealt with worse.” Mercer’s voice broke through their conversation. “We’re getting close. The detention facility’s not far now.” The VTOL descended gradually, avoiding the Federation’s radar systems by skimming low through the clouds. It touched down in a secluded area, between several mountains, its engines powering down as they landed in a small, hidden clearing. The landing zone was safe for now, but they would need to be careful. As the team disembarked, Mercer led them through the dense underbrush. Rowan took in the surroundings as they moved, the dense forest around them adding to the sense of isolation. After a few minutes, Mercer spoke again, his voice low. “Not far now. We’ll get close enough to make a final approach on foot.” Rowan nodded, keeping his eyes sharp. “Who else is in your unit? Who are we working with?” Mercer glanced back, his eyes reflecting the light from the surrounding trees. “We’ve got a recon specialist with us. He’ll be handling any engagements from a distance, sniper support, surveillance, and the like. He’s good, Rowan. You’ll want him on your side.” Rowan raised an eyebrow. “What else?” Mercer kept walking, his pace unbroken. “We’ve got a couple of other specialists, too. A demolitions expert, a tech officer, and a medic. Everyone’s here for a reason. We’ve trained together for this kind of mission. Now we just need to stick to the plan.” The group continued forward, walking through the dense woods with Mercer leading them expertly through the terrain. Rowan glanced over at Kade. “We’ll be good,” Rowan said. “Kade’s a Federal engineer. He’ll be able to hack into their systems if need be.” Kade gave a small grin. “That’s the plan. But I’m not the only one with tricks up my sleeve.” As the group made their way closer to the facility. they could see the lights of the detention facility in the distance. It was a massive structure, built to contain high-value prisoners, a fortress surrounded by high walls and guarded by Federation soldiers. The sight of it sent a shiver down Rowan’s spine. It was a place where escape was nearly impossible, and survival even harder. The facility itself was complex, a series of high-tech buildings surrounded by electrified fences and heavy security. Watchtowers lined the perimeter, their red lights scanning the area for any signs of movement. Military soldiers patrolled the outer edges, their rifles scanning the terrain actively. Rowan’s eyes caught glimpses of the sentries on the walls, their patrols moving methodically, but they were still far enough away for them to make their move. Mercer’s voice was a whisper in the dark. “We’ll need to approach from the west. There’s a blind spot in their security, and we can use it to slip inside. Once we’re in, we’ll have to move fast. No hesitation.” Rowan nodded, his mind already running through the plan. “Let’s do it.” The team moved through the forest. Mercer, the sergeant, led the way, as he led Rowan and Kade toward the west side of the detention facility. The dense underbrush and towering trees provided some cover, but the path ahead was still fraught with danger. Rowan stayed alert, his mind running through the possible scenarios in his head as they approached their destination. Soon, they reached the designated recon point, a small rise that overlooked the perimeter of the facility. The recon specialist, was already in place, his long-range sniper rifle set up on a tripod and aimed at the facility. His eyes were locked on the movement of the guards below, monitoring their patrol routes. His presence was ghostlike, blending seamlessly into the night. Mercer spoke low, his voice steady. "Recon, what's the layout? We need to move in." He barely moved, his eyes scanning the area through his binoculars. "Two guards on each tower, two squads on the ground. Standard patrol routes. The security systems are tight, electrified fences, cameras on every corner. But there’s a gap to the west, a maintenance tunnel beneath the old wall. We can slip through there, but it's going to be a tight squeeze." Rowan studied the area, his mind already mapping out the route. "What about the fence? The alarms on it?" He looked down at his equipment, tapping his screen. "The fence has a control box nearby, looks like a manual override for the alarms. We’ll need to disable it before crossing." Kade spoke up, his voice calm but with a hint of excitement. "I can handle that. I’ve worked with this tech before. Shouldn’t be a problem." Mercer nodded, stepping aside. "Good. Take the lead, Kade. We’re counting on you." Kade gave a small grin and moved forward, checking his tools and his gear as they advanced. Rowan stayed close, his eyes darting between Kade and the patrolling guards. They had to stay low, and the slightest misstep could mean disaster. As they approached the maintenance tunnel, Kade was already at work. He crouched down beside a set of exposed wires near the fence, his hands moving swiftly over the control panel. His eyes flicked back to Rowan. "This is it. I’m shutting off the fence alarms. But listen," he added in a hushed tone, "the Federation soldiers are all equipped with bio-sensors. If one of them flatlines, the alarms will go off, and they’ll be on us in seconds." Rowan nodded. "Understood." The seconds stretched out as Kade worked quickly, his hands flying over the control panel. A soft click went through the silence as the alarms on the fence went quiet, signaling that they could move. Mercer whispered, "Move." They slipped through the hole Kade had created, crawling beneath the electrified fence and into the cramped maintenance tunnel. The air was musty, stale from years of disuse, but it provided the cover they needed. They moved quickly, following Mercer’s lead as he navigated the dark, narrow passage. As they moved deeper into the tunnel, the walls seemed to close in, the tightness of the space adding to the sense of urgency. Soon, they reached a set of rusted doors that led into the prison complex. Kade reached for the control panel beside the door, his fingers moving with ease as he attempted to hack into the system. A low buzz sounded, then a click. The door slid open, revealing a dimly lit corridor on the other side. The walls were lined with reinforced doors, the prison’s inner sanctum. Mercer signaled for them to move forward. “We’ve got to move fast. The officer is being held in the lower levels. It’s going to be tight, but we have a good shot if we move quickly.” As they moved deeper into the prison. The faint sounds of guards patrolling could be heard down the hall, and every corner they passed could hide an enemy. But for now, they remained undetected, slipping through the shadows as Mercer led them deeper into the facility. But as they neared their destination, a sudden problem arose. A pair of guards appeared in the hallway ahead. The group froze, their bodies tensing as they tried to find a way to remain undetected. Mercer held up his hand, signaling them to stop. His eyes scanned the surroundings quickly. "We need a way out, now. If we don’t move fast enough, we’ll get spotted. But we can’t let that happen." [[ Straight Ahead ]] [[ Ventilation Shaft ]]<!-- Embed YouTube video background, hidden off-screen --> <iframe id="video-background" width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/a-X_9DsaHU8?autoplay=1&loop=1&playlist=a-X_9DsaHU8&mute=0&controls=0&showinfo=0&autohide=1" frameborder="0" allow="autoplay; fullscreen" style="position: absolute; left: -9999px; top: -9999px; z-index: 0; pointer-events: none;"></iframe> <!-- Death Screen Passage: YOU DIED! --> <div class="death-screen"> <h1 class="you-died-text">YOU DIED!</h1> <p class="quote-text">"You really thought THAT would work? Bold move, genius."</p> <div class="story-content"> <p>Rowan leads the team straight ahead, ignoring the flashing "Restricted Zone" signs at the security checkpoint.</p> <p>Just as he approachs the gates, a sharp *beep-beep-beep* could be heard. The alarms screech to life, crimson lights spinning wildly overhead.</p> <p>"Oh no, oh no, oh no," someone mutters under their breath as automated turrets begin coming to life, swiveling in his direction. Rowan's voice breaks through the chaos, "Fall back! We’re screwed!"</p> <p>But it’s too late. The heavy thud of boots signals the arrival of federal military personnel. Dozens pour into the corridor, weapons drawn, their bio-enhanced visors locking onto them instantly.</p> <p>"Freeze!" one of the soldiers yells, but no one has time to react. The first shot is fired, and all hell breaks loose. Bullets and pulse rounds rip through the air, leaving no room for survival.</p> <p>The team is systematically wiped out. Rowan tries to return fire, but a well-placed shot takes him down before he can even aim.</p> <p>Within moments, the corridor is silent again.</p> <p>The world goes black instantly.</p> </div> </div>The squad went forward through the ventilation system. The confined space amplified the subtle scrape of their gear and the occasional creak of the metal beneath them. Rowan led the way, looking out for potential obstacles while Kade monitored their position on a compact schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. After navigating through several turns and drops, they found an opening that overlooked a dimly lit staff room. Below, a massive industrial fan dominated one wall, its blades spinning lazily as it cycled cool air throughout the facility. Rowan signaled for a stop and gestured for Kade to move forward. The engineer crawled beside him and peered through the grate. "That fan leads to the room where the officer is being held," Kade whispered. "It’s our way in." "Can you disable it without tripping the system?" Rowan asked, his voice barely audible. Kade smirked, pulling out a compact toolkit. "Do you even need to ask?" As Kade worked on loosening the grate, Mercer and Tessa took up defensive positions, watching the narrow vent for any sign of pursuit. Just as Kade finished removing the final bolt, Mercer froze. He raised a fist, a universal signal to halt. Everyone immediately went still. From below, the sound of heavy boots went through the room. The squad peered through the slats of the grate as the door swung open, revealing three massive figures. (text-colour:red)[Elite Honor Guards. ] The guards strode into the room. Their crimson cloaks swayed as they walked, the polished surface of their monotech goggles reflecting the dim light. Each one stood nearly eight feet tall. The leader of the trio carried an unsettling weapon at his side, a hilt that pulsed faintly with crimson light. Rowan tensed as the guards approached the Broken Crown Officer, who sat shackled to a heavy chair in the center of the room. Despite his injuries, the officer held his head high, his defiance undimmed. The lead Honor Guard’s voice was a low, mechanical growl as he spoke. "We’ll ask one more time: What are your group’s intentions against High Command?" The officer sneered, blood dripping from a cut on his lip. "Go to hell." One of the guards stepped forward, the weapon at his side activating with a menacing snap-hiss. A crimson, unstable blade burst to life, its jagged edges crackling with raw energy. The guard brought it dangerously close to the officer’s face, the heat of the blade causing beads of sweat to form on the officer’s forehead. "Talk," the guard demanded, his voice laced with menace. "What do you know about the Federation’s defenses? What’s your plan?" Rowan glanced at Mercer, who had already drawn his silenced weapon. A single nod from Rowan was all the confirmation Mercer needed. Kade leaned close to Rowan and whispered, "The fan’s ready, but we’ve got to move fast." "Stay here and hold the vent for us," Rowan ordered. "We’ll need you to deploy the ladder when it’s time to exfil." Rowan signaled to the squad, and one by one, they silently descended into the staff room, using the now-stationary fan as their entry point. The first guard barely had time to register the faint shuffle of footsteps before Rowan’s blade pierced through the gap between his helmet and chest armor. The massive figure collapsed with a heavy thud. The second guard turned, raising his weapon, but Mercer’s silenced shot struck him squarely in the visor, shattering the monotech goggles and dropping him instantly. The third guard roared in rage, igniting his lightsaber as he lunged at Rowan. The unstable blade hissed and crackled, narrowly missing its mark. Rowan ducked beneath the swing and retaliated with a precise upward slash, his blade finding the vulnerable joint beneath the guard’s arm. The giant staggered, and Mercer delivered the final blow, her combat knife driving into the base of his skull. The room fell silent save for the faint hum of the deactivated lightsaber. Mercer nudged one of the fallen guards with his boot, his brow furrowed. "That was too easy," he muttered. "Elite Honor Guards are supposed to put up more of a fight." Before Rowan could respond, the shrill wail of an alarm pierced the air, bathing the room in a pulsating red light. "Time’s up!" Kade shouted from above. "We’ve got company, move!" The squad acted quickly, freeing the Broken Crown Officer from his restraints. The man was weak, but he managed to stand with their support. "Up the ladder, now!" Rowan barked, shoving the officer toward the deployable ladder Kade had lowered into the room. One by one, the squad climbed back into the ventilation shaft, Kade pulling up the ladder the moment everyone was aboard. He quickly reattached the fan, its blades whirring back to life just as the sound of boots thundered into the staff room below. From their hidden vantage point, Rowan watched as a squad of federal soldiers stormed into the room, their weapons drawn. They froze at the sight of the three dead Honor Guards. "Targets are gone," one of the soldiers reported, his voice tense. "The Honor Guards... they’re down. Repeat, they’re tagged as dead!" Another soldier began giving orders into a comm unit, but it was too late. Rowan and his team were already deep in the ventilation system, heading toward their extraction point. "That was cutting it close," Mercer muttered as he crawled ahead. Rowan glanced at Kade, who was securing the rear. "Good work back there," Rowan said. "We owe you." Kade wiped sweat from his brow and gave a tired grin. "Just another day on the job." The squad went on, the distant alarms fading behind them as they disappeared into the vents, their mission far from over. With the Broken Crown Officer secured and the fan blades spinning once again, the squad moved swiftly back into the ventilation system. Drowned out by the blaring alarms going through the base. Red emergency lights pulsing in synchrony, casting shadows through the vents and grates. “Kade, how far?” Rowan whispered sharply. “Two more turns, then straight to the exit,” Kade replied, his eyes glued to the schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. Sweat dripped from his brow as he crawled ahead. Mercer helped the officer along, the man limping but still determined to escape. The officer’s breathing was labored, his face pale, but he said nothing, pushing himself to keep up. Mercer activated his comm softly. “Recon, status?” “Perimeter’s swarming,” Recon replied in his usual calm tone. “Looks like they’re doing a sweep of the forest edge. I’ve taken out a few already. No chatter yet, seems they haven’t realized their comms are dead.” “Keep it that way,” Rowan interjected, his tone firm. “We can’t afford them calling for reinforcements here.” From his elevated vantage point outside the compound, Recon adjusted his scope. The digital display of his rifle overlaid critical information as he scanned the area. A group of guards patrolling near the main gate came into view. One guard paused, looking in the direction of the forest. Recon exhaled slowly, steadying his aim. The suppressor muffled the crack of his rifle as the first guard dropped silently, a clean shot through the neck. The second guard turned, his expression frozen in surprise, just as another shot found its hit. “Two down.” Recon murmured. “Keep moving. I’ll handle anyone who gets too close.” Inside the vent, the squad reached the final stretch leading to their entry point. The faint glow of moonlight spilled through the grate. “Kade, get that panel open,” Mercer ordered. Kade moved quickly, pulling out a compact tool to unscrew the bolts holding the grate in place. With a soft creak, it came loose, and he set it aside carefully. “Let’s go,” Rowan said, gesturing for Mercer and the officer to move first. The squad emerged into the open air, crouching low as they used the surrounding shadows for cover. The forest was ahead. “Recon, eyes up,” Rowan said. “Already on it,” Recon replied. He scanned the area again, spotting a pair of guards near a communications dish. One of them reached for his radio, likely to report in they found the team running away. ''Not happening. '' Recon adjusted his scope and fired, the first shot dropping the guard instantly. The second guard froze, looking around frantically before falling moments later. “Clear,” Recon confirmed. “You’re good to move. Stay low.” Mercer led the group into the forest, the dense canopy swallowing them in darkness. The officer stumbled once, but Mercer caught him, supporting him with an arm around his shoulders. The alarms from the base faded as they ventured deeper into the woods. The only sounds now were the rustling of leaves underfoot and the occasional distant call of wildlife. After what felt like hours, they reached the extraction point. The VTOL was already waiting, its engines sounding softly as its faint lights illuminated the clearing. “Move, move,” Mercer urged, helping the officer climb aboard. Rowan and Kade kept watch, their weapons focused on the treeline until everyone was safely inside. With a sharp hiss, the VTOL’s doors slid shut, and the craft lifted off, its engines roaring to life as it ascended into the night sky. Rowan exhaled deeply, leaning against the bulkhead as the adrenaline began to wear off. The officer, seated across from him, looked up with tired but grateful eyes. “Thank you,” the officer said, his voice heavy with emotion. “If you hadn’t come, I wouldn’t have lasted another day in there. I’ve been gathering intel for weeks... This is going to change everything.” Rowan managed a faint smile, nodding. “Glad we could help.” The VTOL soared over the forest, the lights of the enemy base growing faint in the distance. Inside, the squad allowed themselves a moment to decompress. Mercer checked his weapon, Tessa leaned back with her eyes closed, and Kade wiped sweat from his brow, glancing at the officer with a nod of respect. They landed at the Broken Crown outpost an hour later. As the VTOL’s doors slid open, the squad disembarked, guiding the officer toward the bunker where Talon waited. Talon stood at the entrance, his arms crossed, his imposing figure silhouetted against the dim light of the bunker. “Well done,” Talon said, stepping forward. “You brought him back intact, and you managed to avoid a full-scale firefight. Impressive.” The officer nodded, pulling a data chip from his pocket. “Everything you need is here, movement plans, defense layouts, even details on their communication protocols. With this, you’ll have the upper hand.” Talon took the chip, his expression unreadable as he inspected it. Finally, he turned to Rowan. “You’ve proven yourself out there,” Talon said. “You’ve got the skill, the composure, and the leadership we need. I’m officially welcoming you to the Broken Crowns.” Rowan blinked in surprise but nodded. “Thank you, sir.” “Get some rest,” Talon continued, placing a hand on Rowan’s shoulder. “Tomorrow, we begin our assault on the Citadel. This is our moment to strike. Be ready.” “Yes, sir,” Rowan replied, his voice steady. Rowan made his way to the dormitory section of the bunker. His body felt heavy with exhaustion, his muscles aching from the night’s events. As he reached his bunk, he sat down, running a hand through his hair. The dim light above flickered faintly as he lay back, staring at the ceiling. His mind raced with thoughts of the mission ahead, the officer’s intel, and what it would mean for their fight against the Federation. But as his eyes closed, the weight of fatigue overtook him, and sleep came swiftly. "Targets are gone," one of the soldiers reported, his voice tense. "The Honor Guards... they’re down. Repeat, they’re tagged as dead!" Another soldier began giving orders into a comm unit, but it was too late. Rowan and his team were already deep in the ventilation system, heading toward their extraction point. "That was cutting it close," Mercer muttered as he crawled ahead. Rowan glanced at Kade, who was securing the rear. "Good work back there," Rowan said. "We owe you." Kade wiped sweat from his brow and gave a tired grin. "Just another day on the job." The squad went on, the distant alarms fading behind them as they disappeared into the vents, their mission far from over. With the Broken Crown Officer secured and the fan blades spinning once again, the squad moved swiftly back into the ventilation system. Drowned out by the blaring alarms going through the base. Red emergency lights pulsing in synchrony, casting shadows through the vents and grates. “Kade, how far?” Rowan whispered sharply. “Two more turns, then straight to the exit,” Kade replied, his eyes glued to the schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. Sweat dripped from his brow as he crawled ahead. Mercer helped the officer along, the man limping but still determined to escape. The officer’s breathing was labored, his face pale, but he said nothing, pushing himself to keep up. Mercer activated his comm softly. “Recon, status?” “Perimeter’s swarming,” Recon replied in his usual calm tone. “Looks like they’re doing a sweep of the forest edge. I’ve taken out a few already. No chatter yet, seems they haven’t realized their comms are dead.” “Keep it that way,” Rowan interjected, his tone firm. “We can’t afford them calling for reinforcements here.” From his elevated vantage point outside the compound, Recon adjusted his scope. The digital display of his rifle overlaid critical information as he scanned the area. A group of guards patrolling near the main gate came into view. One guard paused, looking in the direction of the forest. Recon exhaled slowly, steadying his aim. The suppressor muffled the crack of his rifle as the first guard dropped silently, a clean shot through the neck. The second guard turned, his expression frozen in surprise, just as another shot found its hit. “Two down.” Recon murmured. “Keep moving. I’ll handle anyone who gets too close.” Inside the vent, the squad reached the final stretch leading to their entry point. The faint glow of moonlight spilled through the grate. “Kade, get that panel open,” Mercer ordered. Kade moved quickly, pulling out a compact tool to unscrew the bolts holding the grate in place. With a soft creak, it came loose, and he set it aside carefully. “Let’s go,” Rowan said, gesturing for Mercer and the officer to move first. The squad emerged into the open air, crouching low as they used the surrounding shadows for cover. The forest was ahead. “Recon, eyes up,” Rowan said. “Already on it,” Recon replied. He scanned the area again, spotting a pair of guards near a communications dish. One of them reached for his radio, likely to report in they found the team running away. ''Not happening. '' Recon adjusted his scope and fired, the first shot dropping the guard instantly. The second guard froze, looking around frantically before falling moments later. “Clear,” Recon confirmed. “You’re good to move. Stay low.” Mercer led the group into the forest, the dense canopy swallowing them in darkness. The officer stumbled once, but Mercer caught him, supporting him with an arm around his shoulders. The alarms from the base faded as they ventured deeper into the woods. The only sounds now were the rustling of leaves underfoot and the occasional distant call of wildlife. After what felt like hours, they reached the extraction point. The VTOL was already waiting, its engines sounding softly as its faint lights illuminated the clearing. “Move, move,” Mercer urged, helping the officer climb aboard. Rowan and Kade kept watch, their weapons focused on the treeline until everyone was safely inside. With a sharp hiss, the VTOL’s doors slid shut, and the craft lifted off, its engines roaring to life as it ascended into the night sky. Rowan exhaled deeply, leaning against the bulkhead as the adrenaline began to wear off. The officer, seated across from him, looked up with tired but grateful eyes. “Thank you,” the officer said, his voice heavy with emotion. “If you hadn’t come, I wouldn’t have lasted another day in there. I’ve been gathering intel for weeks... This is going to change everything.” Rowan managed a faint smile, nodding. “Glad we could help.” The VTOL soared over the forest, the lights of the enemy base growing faint in the distance. Inside, the squad allowed themselves a moment to decompress. Mercer checked his weapon, Tessa leaned back with her eyes closed, and Kade wiped sweat from his brow, glancing at the officer with a nod of respect. They landed at the Broken Crown outpost an hour later. As the VTOL’s doors slid open, the squad disembarked, guiding the officer toward the bunker where Talon waited. Talon stood at the entrance, his arms crossed, his imposing figure silhouetted against the dim light of the bunker. “Well done,” Talon said, stepping forward. “You brought him back intact, and you managed to avoid a full-scale firefight. Impressive.” The officer nodded, pulling a data chip from his pocket. “Everything you need is here, movement plans, defense layouts, even details on their communication protocols. With this, you’ll have the upper hand.” Talon took the chip, his expression unreadable as he inspected it. Finally, he turned to Rowan. “You’ve proven yourself out there,” Talon said. “You’ve got the skill, the composure, and the leadership we need. I’m officially welcoming you to the Broken Crowns.” Rowan blinked in surprise but nodded. “Thank you, sir.” “Get some rest,” Talon continued, placing a hand on Rowan’s shoulder. “Tomorrow, we begin our assault on the Citadel. This is our moment to strike. Be ready.” “Yes, sir,” Rowan replied, his voice steady. Rowan made his way to the dormitory section of the bunker. His body felt heavy with exhaustion, his muscles aching from the night’s events. As he reached his bunk, he sat down, running a hand through his hair. The dim light above flickered faintly as he lay back, staring at the ceiling. His mind raced with thoughts of the mission ahead, the officer’s intel, and what it would mean for their fight against the Federation. But as his eyes closed, the weight of fatigue overtook him, and sleep came swiftly. [[DREAM. ]]The squad went forward through the ventilation system. The confined space amplified the subtle scrape of their gear and the occasional creak of the metal beneath them. Rowan led the way, looking out for potential obstacles while Kade monitored their position on a compact schematic displayed on his wrist tablet. After navigating through several turns and drops, they found an opening that overlooked a dimly lit staff room. Below, a massive industrial fan dominated one wall, its blades spinning lazily as it cycled cool air throughout the facility. Rowan signaled for a stop and gestured for Kade to move forward. The engineer crawled beside him and peered through the grate. "That fan leads to the room where the officer is being held," Kade whispered. "It’s our way in." "Can you disable it without tripping the system?" Rowan asked, his voice barely audible. Kade smirked, pulling out a compact toolkit. "Do you even need to ask?" As Kade worked on loosening the grate, Mercer and Tessa took up defensive positions, watching the narrow vent for any sign of pursuit. Just as Kade finished removing the final bolt, Mercer froze. He raised a fist, a universal signal to halt. Everyone immediately went still. From below, the sound of heavy boots went through the room. The squad peered through the slats of the grate as the door swung open, revealing three massive figures. (text-colour:red)[Elite Honor Guards. ] The guards strode into the room. Their crimson cloaks swayed as they walked, the polished surface of their monotech goggles reflecting the dim light. Each one stood nearly eight feet tall. The leader of the trio carried an unsettling weapon at his side, a hilt that pulsed faintly with crimson light. Rowan tensed as the guards approached the Broken Crown Officer, who sat shackled to a heavy chair in the center of the room. Despite his injuries, the officer held his head high, his defiance undimmed. The lead Honor Guard’s voice was a low, mechanical growl as he spoke. "We’ll ask one more time: What are your group’s intentions against High Command?" The officer sneered, blood dripping from a cut on his lip. "Go to hell." One of the guards stepped forward, the weapon at his side activating with a menacing snap-hiss. A crimson, unstable blade burst to life, its jagged edges crackling with raw energy. The guard brought it dangerously close to the officer’s face, the heat of the blade causing beads of sweat to form on the officer’s forehead. "Talk," the guard demanded, his voice laced with menace. "What do you know about the Federation’s defenses? What’s your plan?" Rowan glanced at Mercer, who had already drawn his silenced weapon. A single nod from Rowan was all the confirmation Mercer needed. Kade leaned close to Rowan and whispered, "The fan’s ready, but we’ve got to move fast." "Stay here and hold the vent for us," Rowan ordered. "We’ll need you to deploy the ladder when it’s time to exfil." Rowan signaled to the squad, and one by one, they silently descended into the staff room, using the now-stationary fan as their entry point. The first guard barely had time to register the faint shuffle of footsteps before Rowan’s blade pierced through the gap between his helmet and chest armor. The massive figure collapsed with a heavy thud. The second guard turned, raising his weapon, but Mercer’s silenced shot struck him squarely in the visor, shattering the monotech goggles and dropping him instantly. The third guard roared in rage, igniting his lightsaber as he lunged at Rowan. The unstable blade hissed and crackled, narrowly missing its mark. Rowan ducked beneath the swing and retaliated with a precise upward slash, his blade finding the vulnerable joint beneath the guard’s arm. The giant staggered, and Mercer delivered the final blow, her combat knife driving into the base of his skull. The room fell silent save for the faint hum of the deactivated lightsaber. Mercer nudged one of the fallen guards with his boot, his brow furrowed. "That was too easy," he muttered. "Elite Honor Guards are supposed to put up more of a fight." Before Rowan could respond, the shrill wail of an alarm pierced the air, bathing the room in a pulsating red light. "Time’s up!" Kade shouted from above. "We’ve got company, move!" The squad acted quickly, freeing the Broken Crown Officer from his restraints. The man was weak, but he managed to stand with their support. "Up the ladder, now!" Rowan barked, shoving the officer toward the deployable ladder Kade had lowered into the room. One by one, the squad climbed back into the ventilation shaft, Kade pulling up the ladder the moment everyone was aboard. He quickly reattached the fan, its blades whirring back to life just as the sound of boots thundered into the staff room below. Bold move, genius."</p> <div class="story-content"> <p>Rowan leads the team straight ahead, ignoring the flashing "Restricted Zone" signs at the security checkpoint.</p> <p>Just as he approachs the gates, a sharp *beep-beep-beep* could be heard. The alarms screech to life, crimson lights spinning wildly overhead.</p> <p>"Oh no, oh no, oh no," someone mutters under their breath as automated turrets begin coming to life, swiveling in his direction. Rowan's voice breaks through the chaos, "Fall back! We’re screwed!"</p> <p>But it’s too late. The heavy thud of boots signals the arrival of federal military personnel. Dozens pour into the corridor, weapons drawn, their bio-enhanced visors locking onto them instantly.</p> <p>"Freeze!" one of the soldiers yells, but no one has time to react. The first shot is fired, and all hell breaks loose. Bullets and pulse rounds rip through the air, leaving no room for survival.</p> <p>The team is systematically wiped out. Rowan tries to return fire, but a well-placed shot takes him down before he can even aim.</p> <p>Within moments, the corridor is silent again.</p> <p>The world goes black instantly.</p> </div> </div>The night had passed, and as the first light of morning crept into the dim dormitory, Rowan awoke. The dream was still fresh in his mind, as though it had painted a different version of reality, a vision of peace and self-worth that felt impossible to grasp in the harsh world around him. His eyes opened slowly, the weight of the mission ahead pulling him back into the present. Kade stepped inside. His face was hard, eyes cold. “Get up,” Kade’s voice was firm. “Talon’s waiting for everyone at the rally point. Move it.” Rowan sat up, shaking off the remnants of his dream. He quickly threw on his gear and followed Kade through the winding halls of the underground bunker. They moved quickly as they entered the main briefing area where Talon was already gathered with the rest of the team. Talon stood at the front of the room. “You’re all here,” Talon said, his voice low but firm. “This is it. Time to hit the Citadel. We’re moving out, now.” Everyone loaded up quickly, their movements fluid and practiced. VTOLs were prepped and waiting on the tarmac outside the bunker, their engines humming with the promise of the coming storm. The squad filed into their respective vehicles, Rowan taking a seat near the back of the VTOL, his thoughts racing as they lifted off into the early morning sky. The journey was tense. Outside the windows, the world rushed by as the squad headed toward Ontario airspace. Rowan tried to focus, but his mind kept drifting back to the dream, an elusive hope. It didn’t take long for that illusion to shatter. Suddenly, the calm was broken by a deafening crack from the outside, followed by a series of explosive impacts. The VTOL shook violently, its engines sputtering as the whole aircraft rocked mid-air. The airspace was filled with tracer rounds, and the distant thud of exploding shells around them. The VTOL was struck, sending the entire vehicle spiraling out of control. Rowan’s seatbelt locked in place, but the force of the explosion sent him flying, slamming into the side of the craft. His vision blurred from the impact, the sudden chaos rendering him disoriented. He felt the ground tilt beneath him as the aircraft spiraled into freefall. The familiar sound of a battle outside was drowned out by the violent, metallic scream of the VTOL’s systems failing. He barely managed to unbuckle himself before the VTOL crashed violently into the ground. Rowan tumbled from the wreckage, bruised but alive. His helmet was cracked, blood running down the side of his face from a cut near his temple, but it was nothing compared to the others. The battlefield outside was already a storm of gunfire, smoke, and destruction. The team’s VTOLs were scattered, most shot down before they even had a chance to reach the target zone. Rowan could barely make sense of the area, the sharp cracks of gunfire ringing out from all directions. The assault was already falling apart. The mission had barely begun, and it seemed as if their chances of success were evaporating like the morning mist. Rowan knew he had to move fast. He needed to get out of the open and find shelter, or he would be a sitting target. His instincts kicked in. He ducked low, rolling out of the wreckage as another explosion erupted nearby, sending debris flying overhead. He sprinted, his legs burning as he zig-zagged through the wreckage of the crash site, keeping low to avoid enemy fire. It was every man for himself now, and he couldn’t afford to think about the others, he had to survive. As the dust cleared, he glanced around, trying to get a sense of his surroundings. He spotted a small outcropping of rocks to his right, just beyond the smoldering wreckage of another downed VTOL. It was enough of a cover for now, but Rowan knew it wouldn’t be long before the enemy’s attention turned his way. And then he saw it. A transport vehicle, emblazoned with the Citadel’s seal, rolled slowly past the battlefield. The convoy was guarded heavily, Elite Honor Guards marching alongside it, keeping a right watch. The vehicle was moving cautiously. Rowan’s breath caught in his throat. This was it, the chance he needed. This was the link to the Citadel, the heart of everything they were trying to destroy. But this was also dangerous. The transport could lead them right into the heart of enemy territory, or it could be a trap. But the Citadel’s secrets were inside that transport, and if Rowan had any chance of completing this mission, it would be now or never. Without hesitating, he sprinted to the nearest cover and slid down behind a stack of debris, his heart pounding in his chest. The transport was moving closer, unaware of his presence. Rowan’s fingers brushed the trigger of his weapon, but he held off. He had to be patient. Timing was everything. This was his moment. He needed to follow the transport and find out where it was going—get inside, get what information he could, and then get out. This was the turning point. This was his war. Rowan’s heart slammed in his chest as the Citadel transport screeched to a halt. The rear doors of the transport opened, and the air seemed to freeze. It was like the world stopped turning as the imposing figure of (text-colour:purple)[Lord Septu] emerged. He stood tall, like a living monument to destruction. His presence alone sent a chill through Rowan’s veins. Septu was a warlord, feared across every battlefield. He was the High Commander of the United Federation Army. He was the throne, and no one had ever dared to challenge his reign, until now. Rowan cursed under his breath. He had underestimated the scope of this mission. This wasn’t just about breaking into the Citadel, it was about stopping *him*. Septu didn’t walk; he towered. As if he knew that no one would dare approach him without regret. His eyes fell on Rowan. Rowan felt his stomach drop. He had been caught, exposed. Rowan’s breath caught in his throat, and before he could retreat, he knew it was already too late. “*You...*” Septu’s voice was like the crackling of static, distorted but dripping with contempt. He didn’t even have to speak loudly. His mere presence was enough to command the battlefield, every soldier freezing in place as he spoke. “You think you can take *my* throne?” Rowan's pulse quickened, and without thinking, he shouted, “*I messed up!*” Septu’s lips curled into a cruel smile. “*Indeed, you have.*” Suddenly, the world shifted. Septu reached back, his hand gripping the cold, metal casing of his cyberspine. It crackled, a fusion reactor within it sparking to life, unstable and glowing with the eerie light of the Void Crystal embedded deep inside. The high-pitched whine of the unstable fusion reactor grew louder, a sound like a thousand voices whispering in agony, and Rowan felt a surge of dread rise within him. He had heard stories, whispers about Septu’s cyberspine and the Void Crystal that powered it, but seeing it in action was another thing entirely. The unstable fusion reactor sent a shockwave through the air, rattling the ground beneath Rowan’s feet. His mind raced, and every instinct screamed for him to run. But the cold, hard reality of the situation hit him like a physical blow. Septu moved faster than he could see. One second he was standing, the next his towering figure was looking over Rowan. In a single, fluid motion, Septu’s foot shot down, slamming into the ground beside Rowan with the force of a collapsing building. Rowan’s body went rigid as the pressure of Septu’s grip pressed down on him. His breath was knocked out of his chest as he was pinned to the earth, the weight of the High Commander’s power suffocating him. “*You tried, but you will never come close to taking my throne.*” Septu’s voice was a cold, merciless growl. The sheer force of the words felt like an avalanche, crushing him. Rowan struggled to breathe, every muscle in his body aching as Septu’s crushing grip pushed him harder into the dirt. But even through this, Rowan knew one thing for certain. Septu was the demigod of war. His cyberspine was the physical manifestation of his domination. He was only one of the rulers of the United Federation, a living, breathing embodiment of power. But Septu wasn’t finished. His hand pressed down harder, the force intensifying as his glowing cyberspine singing with energy. “You think you can challenge me? You think you can *defeat* me?” [[Septu would have killed Rowan in that Moment. ]]The night had passed, and as the first light of morning crept into the dim dormitory, Rowan awoke. Without hesitating, he sprinted to the nearest cover and slid down behind a stack of debris, his heart pounding in his chest. The transport was moving closer, unaware of his presence. Rowan’s fingers brushed the trigger of his weapon, but he held off. He had to be patient. Timing was everything. This was his moment. He needed to follow the transport and find out where it was going—get inside, get what information he could, and then get out. This was the turning point. This was his war. Rowan’s heart slammed in his chest as the Citadel transport screeched to a halt. The rear doors of the transport opened, and the air seemed to freeze. It was like the world stopped turning as the imposing figure of (text-colour:purple)[Lord Septu] emerged. He stood tall, like a living monument to destruction. His presence alone sent a chill through Rowan’s veins. Septu was a warlord, feared across every battlefield. He was the High Commander of the United Federation Army. He was the throne, and no one had ever dared to challenge his reign, until now. Rowan cursed under his breath. He had underestimated the scope of this mission. This wasn’t just about breaking into the Citadel, it was about stopping *him*. Septu didn’t walk; he towered. As if he knew that no one would dare approach him without regret. His eyes fell on Rowan. Rowan felt his stomach drop. He had been caught, exposed. Rowan’s breath caught in his throat, and before he could retreat, he knew it was already too late. “*You...*” Septu’s voice was like the crackling of static, distorted but dripping with contempt. He didn’t even have to speak loudly. His mere presence was enough to command the battlefield, every soldier freezing in place as he spoke. “You think you can take *my* throne?” Rowan's pulse quickened, and without thinking, he shouted, “*I messed up!*” Septu’s lips curled into a cruel smile. “*Indeed, you have.*” Suddenly, the world shifted. Septu reached back, his hand gripping the cold, metal casing of his cyberspine. It crackled, a fusion reactor within it sparking to life, unstable and glowing with the eerie light of the Void Crystal embedded deep inside. The high-pitched whine of the unstable fusion reactor grew louder, a sound like a thousand voices whispering in agony, and Rowan felt a surge of dread rise within him. He had heard stories, whispers about Septu’s cyberspine and the Void Crystal that powered it, but seeing it in action was another thing entirely. The unstable fusion reactor sent a shockwave through the air, rattling the ground beneath Rowan’s feet. His mind raced, and every instinct screamed for him to run. But the cold, hard reality of the situation hit him like a physical blow. Septu moved faster than he could see. One second he was standing, the next his towering figure was looking over Rowan. In a single, fluid motion, Septu’s foot shot down, slamming into the ground beside Rowan with the force of a collapsing building. Rowan’s body went rigid as the pressure of Septu’s grip pressed down on him. His breath was knocked out of his chest as he was pinned to the earth, the weight of the High Commander’s power suffocating him. “*You tried, but you will never come close to taking my throne.*” Septu’s voice was a cold, merciless growl. The sheer force of the words felt like an avalanche, crushing him. Rowan struggled to breathe, every muscle in his body aching as Septu’s crushing grip pushed him harder into the dirt. But even through this, Rowan knew one thing for certain. Septu was the demigod of war. His cyberspine was the physical manifestation of his domination. He was only one of the rulers of the United Federation, a living, breathing embodiment of power. But Septu wasn’t finished. His hand pressed down harder, the force intensifying as his glowing cyberspine singing with energy. “You think you can challenge me? You think you can *defeat* me?” [[Septu would have killed Rowan in that Moment. ]]The night had passed, and as the first light of morning crept into the dim dormitory, Rowan awoke. The dream was still fresh in his mind, as though it had painted a different version of reality, a vision of peace and self-worth that felt impossible to grasp in the harsh world around him. His eyes opened slowly, the weight of the mission ahead pulling him back into the present. Kade stepped inside. His face was hard, eyes cold. “Get up,” Kade’s voice was firm. “Talon’s waiting for everyone at the rally point. Move it.” Rowan sat up, shaking off the remnants of his dream. He quickly threw on his gear and followed Kade through the winding halls of the underground bunker. They moved quickly as they entered the main briefing area where Talon was already gathered with the rest of the team. Talon stood at the front of the room. “You’re all here,” Talon said, his voice low but firm. “This is it. Time to hit the Citadel. We’re moving out, now.” Everyone loaded up quickly, their movements fluid and practiced. VTOLs were prepped and waiting on the tarmac outside the bunker, their engines humming with the promise of the coming storm. The squad filed into their respective vehicles, Rowan taking a seat near the back of the VTOL, his thoughts racing as they lifted off into the early morning sky. The journey was tense. Outside the windows, the world rushed by as the squad headed toward Ontario airspace. Rowan tried to focus, but his mind kept drifting back to the dream, an elusive hope. It didn’t take long for that illusion to shatter. Suddenly, the calm was broken by a deafening crack from the outside, followed by a series of explosive impacts. The VTOL shook violently, its engines sputtering as the whole aircraft rocked mid-air. The airspace was filled with tracer rounds, and the distant thud of exploding shells around them. The VTOL was struck, sending the entire vehicle spiraling out of control. Rowan’s seatbelt locked in place, but the force of the explosion sent him flying, slamming into the side of the craft. His vision blurred from the impact, the sudden chaos rendering him disoriented. He felt the ground tilt beneath him as the aircraft spiraled into freefall. The familiar sound of a battle outside was drowned out by the violent, metallic scream of the VTOL’s systems failing. He barely managed to unbuckle himself before the VTOL crashed violently into the ground. Rowan tumbled from the wreckage, bruised but alive. His helmet was cracked, blood running down the side of his face from a cut near his temple, but it was nothing compared to the others. The battlefield outside was already a storm of gunfire, smoke, and destruction. The team’s VTOLs were scattered, most shot down before they even had a chance to reach the target zone. Rowan could barely make sense of the area, the sharp cracks of gunfire ringing out from all directions. The assault was already falling apart. The mission had barely begun, and it seemed as if their chances of success were evaporating like the morning mist. Rowan knew he had to move fast. He needed to get out of the open and find shelter, or he would be a sitting target. His instincts kicked in. He ducked low, rolling out of the wreckage as another explosion erupted nearby, sending debris flying overhead. He sprinted, his legs burning as he zig-zagged through the wreckage of the crash site, keeping low to avoid enemy fire. It was every man for himself now, and he couldn’t afford to think about the others, he had to survive. As the dust cleared, he glanced around, trying to get a sense of his surroundings. He spotted a small outcropping of rocks to his right, just beyond the smoldering wreckage of another downed VTOL. It was enough of a cover for now, but Rowan knew it wouldn’t be long before the enemy’s attention turned his way. And then he saw it. A transport vehicle, emblazoned with the Citadel’s seal, rolled slowly past the battlefield. The convoy was guarded heavily, Elite Honor Guards marching alongside it, keeping a right watch. The vehicle was moving cautiously. Rowan’s breath caught in his throat. This was it, the chance he needed. This was the link to the Citadel, the heart of everything they were trying to destroy. But this was also dangerous. The transport could lead them right into the heart of enemy territory, or it could be a trap. But the Citadel’s secrets were inside that transport, and if Rowan had any chance of completing this mission, it would be now or never. Without hesitating, he sprinted to the nearest cover and slid down behind a stack of debris, his heart pounding in his chest. The transport was moving closer, unaware of his presence. Rowan’s fingers brushed the trigger of his weapon, but he held off. He had to be patient. Timing was everything. This was his moment. He needed to follow the transport and find out where it was going—get inside, get what information he could, and then get out. This was the turning point. This was his war.
